| * [Animalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animalia "Animalia") * [Fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi") * [Embryophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte") (land plants) |

A **protist** ( [_PROH-tist_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key")) or **protoctist** is any [eukaryotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote "Eukaryote")[organism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organism "Organism") that is not an [animal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal"), [land plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte"), or [fungus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus"). Protists do not form a [natural group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clade "Clade"), or clade, but are a [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyly "Paraphyly") grouping of all descendants of the [last eukaryotic common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor") excluding land plants, animals, and fungi.

Protists were historically regarded as a separate [taxonomic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomic_rank "Taxonomic rank")[kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology) "Kingdom (biology)") known as **Protista** or **Protoctista**. With the advent of [phylogenetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylogenetic "Phylogenetic") analysis and [electron microscopy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_microscopy "Electron microscopy") studies, the use of Protista as a formal [taxon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxon "Taxon") was gradually abandoned. In modern classifications, protists are spread across several eukaryotic clades called [supergroups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supergroup_(biology) "Supergroup (biology)"), such as [Archaeplastida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeplastida "Archaeplastida") ([photoautotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoautotroph "Photoautotroph") that includes land plants), [SAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAR_supergroup "SAR supergroup"), [Obazoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obazoa "Obazoa") (which includes fungi and animals), [Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa") and "[Excavata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excavata "Excavata")".

Protists represent an extremely large [genetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_diversity "Genetic diversity") and [ecological diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_diversity "Ecological diversity") in all environments, including extreme habitats. Their [diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity"), larger than for all other eukaryotes, has only been discovered in recent decades through the study of [environmental DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA") and is still in the process of being fully described. They are present in all [ecosystems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem "Ecosystem") as important components of the [biogeochemical cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeochemical_cycle "Biogeochemical cycle") and [trophic webs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_web "Trophic web"). They exist abundantly and ubiquitously in a variety of mostly unicellular forms that evolved multiple times independently, such as free-living [algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae "Algae"), [amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebae "Amoebae") and [slime moulds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slime_mould "Slime mould"), or as important [parasites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasite "Parasite"). Together, they compose an amount of biomass that doubles that of animals. They exhibit varied types of nutrition (such as [phototrophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phototrophy "Phototrophy"), [phagotrophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagotrophy "Phagotrophy") or [osmotrophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmotrophy "Osmotrophy")), sometimes combining them (in [mixotrophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixotrophy "Mixotrophy")). They present unique adaptations not present in multicellular animals, fungi or land plants. The study of protists is termed [protistology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protistology "Protistology").

[![Image 3](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png/250px-Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tree_of_Living_Organisms_2.png)

The [tree of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_of_life_(biology) "Tree of life (biology)") showing the position of protists, from which all other eukaryotes evolved.

Protists are a diverse group of [eukaryotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote "Eukaryote") that are primarily [single-celled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-celled "Single-celled") and microscopic and exhibit a wide variety of shapes and life strategies. They have different [life cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle "Biological life cycle"), [trophic levels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_level "Trophic level"), [modes of locomotion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist_locomotion "Protist locomotion"), and [cellular structures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organelle "Organelle").[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simonite-2005-4)[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Harper-2009-5) Although most protists are [unicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicellular "Unicellular"), there is a considerable range of [multicellularity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellularity "Multicellularity") amongst them; some form colonies or [multicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellular "Multicellular") structures visible to the naked eye. The term 'protist' refers to all eukaryotes that are not [animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal"), land plants or [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi"), the three traditional eukaryotic [kingdoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology) "Kingdom (biology)").[[a]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-kingdoms-13)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-O'Malley-2012-14) Because of this definition by exclusion, protists compose a [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyletic "Paraphyletic") group that includes the ancestors of those three kingdoms.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Seb%C3%A9-Pedr%C3%B3s-2017-15)

The names of some protists (called [ambiregnal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ambiregnal "Ambiregnal") protists), because of their mixture of traits similar to both animals and land plants or fungi (e.g., [slime molds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slime_molds "Slime molds") and [flagellated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellate "Flagellate") algae like [euglenids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenid#Classification "Euglenid")), have been published under either or both of the botanical (_[ICNafp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International\_Code\_of\_Nomenclature\_for\_algae,\_fungi,\_and\_plants "International Code of Nomenclature for algae, fungi, and plants")_) and the zoological (_[ICZN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International\_Code\_of\_Zoological\_Nomenclature "International Code of Zoological Nomenclature")_) [codes of nomenclature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Codes_of_nomenclature "Codes of nomenclature").[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Corliss-1995-16)[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Barnes-2001-17)

Protists display a wide range of distinct [morphological types](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology) "Morphology (biology)") that have been used to classify them for practical purposes, although most of these categories do not represent evolutionary cohesive lineages or [clades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clade "Clade") and have instead [evolved independently](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolved_independently "Evolved independently") several times. The most recognizable types are:[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)

*   [Amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebae "Amoebae"). Characterized by their irregular, flexible shapes, these protists move by extending portions of their [cytoplasm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoplasm "Cytoplasm"), known as [pseudopodia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudopodia "Pseudopodia"), to crawl along surfaces.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-De_Bruyn-1947-19) Many groups of amoebae are naked, but [testate amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testate_amoebae "Testate amoebae") and [foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") grow a shell around their [cell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_(biology) "Cell (biology)") made from digested material or surrounding debris. Some, known as [radiolarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria") and [heliozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliozoa "Heliozoa"), have special spherical shapes with microtubule-supported pseudopodia radiating from the cell.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Some amoebae are capable of producing stalked multicellular stages that bear spores, often by aggregating together; these are known as [slime molds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slime_mold "Slime mold").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2012-20) The main clades containing amoebae are [Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa") (including various slime molds and testate amoebae) and [Rhizaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizaria "Rhizaria") (including famous groups such as [foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") and radiolarians, as well as a few testate amoebae).[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2008-21)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2009-22) Even some individual amoebae can grow to giant sizes visible to the naked eye.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-23)[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-24)
*   [Flagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellates "Flagellates"). These protists are equipped with one or more whip-like appendages called [cilia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cilia "Cilia"), [undulipodia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undulipodia "Undulipodia") or [eukaryotic flagella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic_flagellum "Eukaryotic flagellum"),[[b]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-cilia-28) which enable them to swim or [glide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gliding_motility "Gliding motility") freely through the environment. Flagellates are found in all lineages, reflecting that the [common ancestor of all living eukaryotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor") was a flagellate. They usually exhibit two cilia (e.g., in [Provora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provora "Provora"), [Telonemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telonemia "Telonemia"), [Stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stramenopiles "Stramenopiles"), [Alveolata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alveolata "Alveolata"), [Obazoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obazoa "Obazoa") and most [excavates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excavata "Excavata")), but there are a number of flagellate groups with a high number of cilia (such as [Hemimastigophora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemimastigophora "Hemimastigophora") and other excavates).[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Some groups, such as the well-known [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate") and the parasitic [opalinids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opalinid "Opalinid"), have a cell surface covered in rows of cilia that beat rhythmically. A few groups of amoebae have retained their flagella, making them [amoeboflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoeboflagellates "Amoeboflagellates").[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brunet-2021-29)
*   [Algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae "Algae"). They are the [photosynthetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthetic "Photosynthetic") protists, and can be found in most of the main clades, completely intermingled with [heterotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotrophic "Heterotrophic") protists which are traditionally called _[protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa")_.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30) Algae exhibit the most diverse range of morphologies, from single flagellated or coccoid cells (e.g., [cryptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptophytes "Cryptophytes"), [haptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptophyte "Haptophyte"), [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellates "Dinoflagellates"), [chromerids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromerid "Chromerid"), many [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), [ochrophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ochrophyte "Ochrophyte"), [euglenophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenophyte "Euglenophyte")) to amoeboid cells ([chlorarachniophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorarachniophyte "Chlorarachniophyte")) to colonial and multicellular macroscopic forms (e.g., [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae"), some [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), and some [ochrophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ochrophyte "Ochrophyte") such as [kelp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelp "Kelp")).[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-31)
*   Fungus-like protists. Several clades of protists have evolved an appearance similar to [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi") through [hyphae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyphae "Hyphae")-like structures and a [saprophytic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saprophytic "Saprophytic") nutrition. They have evolved multiple times, often very distantly from true fungi (e.g., the [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycete "Oomycete"), [labyrinthulomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labyrinthulomycetes "Labyrinthulomycetes") and [hyphochytrids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyphochytrid "Hyphochytrid"), in Stramenopiles; the [myxomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxomycete "Myxomycete"), in Amoebozoa; the [phytomyxeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytomyxea "Phytomyxea"), in Rhizaria; the [perkinsozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perkinsozoa "Perkinsozoa"), in Alveolata).[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-32)[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-33)
*   [Sporozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sporozoa "Sporozoa"). This category traditionally included [parasitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitic "Parasitic") protists that reproduced via spores (the [apicomplexans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa"), [microsporidians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsporidia "Microsporidia"), [myxozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxozoa "Myxozoa") and [ascetosporeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ascetosporea "Ascetosporea")).[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levine-1980-6) Its current use is restricted to the apicomplexans,[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-1993-34) such as _[Plasmodium falciparum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmodium\_falciparum "Plasmodium falciparum")_, the cause of [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria").[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-35)

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Eukaryotic_diversity_morphological_vs_genetic.png/330px-Eukaryotic_diversity_morphological_vs_genetic.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Eukaryotic_diversity_morphological_vs_genetic.png)

Difference between morphological (A) and genetic (B) view of total eukaryotic diversity. Protists dominate [DNA barcoding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_barcoding "DNA barcoding") analyses, but constitute a minority of catalogued species.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2012-36)

The [species diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species_diversity "Species diversity") of protists is severely underestimated by traditional methods that differentiate species based on [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology) "Morphology (biology)") characteristics. The number of described protist [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species "Species") is very low (ranging from 26,000[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Mora-2011-37) to over 76,000)[[c]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-39) in comparison to the [diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity") of land plants, animals and fungi, which are historically and biologically well-known and studied. The predicted number of species also varies greatly, ranging from 140,000 to 1,600,000, and in several groups the number of predicted species is arbitrarily doubled. Most of these predictions are highly subjective. Molecular techniques such as [environmental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA")[DNA barcoding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_barcoding "DNA barcoding") have revealed a vast diversity of undescribed protists that accounts for the majority of eukaryotic sequences or [operational taxonomic units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operational_taxonomic_unit "Operational taxonomic unit") (OTUs), dwarfing those from land plants, animals and fungi.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2012-36) As such, it is considered that protists dominate eukaryotic diversity.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Burki-2021-40)

Protist phylogeny

One possible topology for the eukaryotic tree of life, with uncertain positions of [ancyromonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancyromonad "Ancyromonad"), [excavates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excavata "Excavata"), [provorans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provora "Provora") and [hemimastigotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemimastigote "Hemimastigote").[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2018-41)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tikhonenkov-2022a-3)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yazaki-2022-42)[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eglit-2024-43) Excavate groups are shown in green. 1 Includes land plants. 2 Includes animals and fungi.

The evolutionary relationships of protists have been explained through [molecular phylogenetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_phylogenetics "Molecular phylogenetics"), the [sequencing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_sequencing "DNA sequencing") of entire [genomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome "Genome") and [transcriptomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcriptome "Transcriptome"), and [electron microscopy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electron_microscopy "Electron microscopy") studies of the [flagellar apparatus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellum "Flagellum") and [cytoskeleton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoskeleton "Cytoskeleton"). New major lineages of protists and novel [biodiversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity") continue to be discovered, resulting in dramatic changes to the eukaryotic tree of life. The newest classification systems of eukaryotes do not recognize the formal [taxonomic ranks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomic_rank "Taxonomic rank") (kingdom, phylum, class, order...) and instead only recognize [clades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clades "Clades") of related organisms, making the classification more stable in the long term and easier to update. In this new [cladistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cladistic "Cladistic") scheme, the protists are divided into various branches informally named [supergroups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supergroup_(biology) "Supergroup (biology)"). Most photosynthetic eukaryotes fall under the [Diaphoretickes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diaphoretickes "Diaphoretickes") clade, which contains the supergroups [Archaeplastida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeplastida "Archaeplastida") (which includes land plants) and [SAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAR_supergroup "SAR supergroup") (including, [Stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stramenopiles "Stramenopiles"), [Alveolata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alveolata "Alveolata") and [Rhizaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizaria "Rhizaria")), as well as the phyla [Telonemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telonemia "Telonemia"), [Cryptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptista "Cryptista") and [Haptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptista "Haptista").[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-44) The animals and fungi fall into the [Amorphea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amorphea "Amorphea") supergroup, which contains the phylum [Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa") and several other protist lineages. Various groups of eukaryotes with primitive cell architecture are collectively known as the "Excavata".[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)

"[Excavata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excavata "Excavata")" is a group that encompasses diverse protists, mostly flagellates, ranging from aerobic and anaerobic predators to phototrophs and heterotrophs.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Madigan-2019-45): 597  The common name 'excavate' refers to the common characteristic of a ventral groove in the cell used for [suspension feeding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suspension_feeding "Suspension feeding"), which is considered to be an ancestral trait present in the [last eukaryotic common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor").[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-46) The "Excavata" is composed of three clades: [Discoba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discoba "Discoba"), [Metamonada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamonada "Metamonada") and [Malawimonadida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malawimonadida "Malawimonadida"), each including 'typical excavates' that are free-living phagotrophic flagellates with the characteristic ventral groove.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-47) According to most phylogenetic analyses, this group is [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyletic "Paraphyletic"),[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eglit-2024-43) with some analyses placing the root of the eukaryote tree within Metamonada.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-48)

Discoba includes three major groups: [Jakobida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jakobida "Jakobida"), [Euglenozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenozoa "Euglenozoa") and [Percolozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Percolozoa "Percolozoa").[[d]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Percolozoa-50) Jakobida are a small group (~20 species) of free-living heterotrophic flagellates, with two cilia, that primarily eat bacteria through suspension feeding; most are aquatic aerobes, with some anaerobic species, found in marine, brackish or fresh water.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017b-51) They are best known for their bacterial-like mitochondrial genomes.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Euglenozoa is a rich (>2,000 species)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) group of flagellates with very different lifestyles, including: the free-living heterotrophic (both osmo- and phagotrophic)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Madigan-2019-45) and photosynthetic [euglenids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenid "Euglenid") (e.g., the [euglenophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenophyte "Euglenophyte"), with chloroplasts originated from green algae); the free-living and parasitic [kinetoplastids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinetoplastid "Kinetoplastid") (such as _[Trypanosoma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trypanosoma "Trypanosoma")_); the deep-sea anaerobic [symbiontids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbiontida "Symbiontida"); and the elusive [diplonemids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplonemid "Diplonemid").[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Kostygov-2021-53) Percolozoa[[d]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Percolozoa-50) (~150 species) are a collection of amoebae, flagellates and amoeboflagellates with complex life cycles, among which are some slime molds ([acrasids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acrasid "Acrasid")).[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-P%C3%A1nek-2017-49) The two clades Euglenozoa and Percolozoa are [sister taxa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sister_group "Sister group"), united under the name [Discicristata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discicristata "Discicristata"), in reference to their [mitochondrial cristae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crista "Crista") shaped like discs.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2022-9) The species _[Tsukubamonas globosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsukubamonas\_globosa "Tsukubamonas globosa")_ is a free-living flagellate whose precise position within Discoba is not yet settled, but is probably more closely related to Discicristata than to Jakobida.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017b-51)

The [metamonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamonad "Metamonad") (Metamonada) are a phylum of completely [anaerobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaerobe "Anaerobe") or [microaerophilic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microaerophilic "Microaerophilic") protozoa, primarily [flagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellate "Flagellate"). Some are [gut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract "Gastrointestinal tract") symbionts of animals such as [termites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Termite "Termite"), others are free-living, and others are parasitic. They include three main clades: [Fornicata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fornicata "Fornicata"), [Parabasalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parabasalia "Parabasalia") and [Preaxostyla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preaxostyla "Preaxostyla").[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Fornicata (>140 species)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2007-38) encompasses the [diplomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplomonad "Diplomonad"), with two [nuclei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus "Cell nucleus") (e.g., _[Giardia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giardia "Giardia")_), and several smaller groups of free-living, commensal and parasitic protists (e.g., _[Carpediemonas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpediemonas "Carpediemonas")_, [retortamonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retortamonad "Retortamonad")).[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Parabasalia (>460 species)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2007-38) is a varied group of anaerobic, mostly endobiotic organisms, ranging from small parasites (like _[Trichomonas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trichomonas "Trichomonas")_) to giant intestinal symbionts with numerous flagella and nuclei found in wood-eating termites and [cockroaches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cockroach "Cockroach").[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Preaxostyla (~140 species) includes the anaerobic and endobiotic [oxymonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxymonad "Oxymonad"), with modified (or completely lost)[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-54)[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Nov%C3%A1k-2023-55)[mitochondria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondria "Mitochondria"), and two genera of free-living microaerophilic bacterivorous flagellates _[Trimastix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimastix "Trimastix")_ and _[Paratrimastix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paratrimastix "Paratrimastix")_, with typical excavate morphology.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Nov%C3%A1k-2023-55)[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-56) Two genera of anaerobic flagellates of recent description and unique cell architecture, _[Barthelona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barthelona "Barthelona")_ and _[Skoliomonas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skoliomonas "Skoliomonas")_, are closely related to the Fornicata.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-57)

The [malawimonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malawimonad "Malawimonad") (Malawimonadida) are a small group (three species) of freshwater or marine suspension-feeding bacterivorous flagellates[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Heiss-2020-58) with typical excavate appearance, closely resembling Jakobida and some metamonads but not phylogenetically close to either in most analyses.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)

_[Giardia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giardia "Giardia")_, a genus of intestinal parasites that cause [giardiasis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giardiasis "Giardiasis") 
*   [![Image 6: Trichomonas vaginalis, the causative agent of trichomoniasis](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Trichomonas_Giemsa_DPDx.JPG/120px-Trichomonas_Giemsa_DPDx.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trichomonas_Giemsa_DPDx.JPG "Trichomonas vaginalis, the causative agent of trichomoniasis")

*   [![Image 7: Trypanosoma cruzi, the causative agent of Chagas disease](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Trypanosoma_cruzi_B.jpg/120px-Trypanosoma_cruzi_B.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trypanosoma_cruzi_B.jpg "Trypanosoma cruzi, the causative agent of Chagas disease")

*   [![Image 8: Euglena, a genus of photosynthetic euglenids](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Two_Euglena.jpg/120px-Two_Euglena.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Two_Euglena.jpg "Euglena, a genus of photosynthetic euglenids")

_[Euglena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglena "Euglena")_, a genus of photosynthetic euglenids

*   [![Image 9: Malawimonas cells, with typical excavate architecture](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Malawimonasms.jpg/120px-Malawimonasms.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Malawimonasms.jpg "Malawimonas cells, with typical excavate architecture")

_[Malawimonas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malawimonas "Malawimonas")_ cells, with typical excavate architecture

[Diaphoretickes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diaphoretickes "Diaphoretickes") includes nearly all photosynthetic eukaryotes. The [SAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAR_supergroup "SAR supergroup") supergroup gathers a colossal diversity of protists. It includes [Stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stramenopile "Stramenopile"), [Alveolata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alveolate "Alveolate") and [Stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizaria "Rhizaria").[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tikhonenkov-2022b-59) Another highly diverse clade within Diaphoretickes is [Archaeplastida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeplastida "Archaeplastida"), which houses [land plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte") and a variety of algae. In addition, three smaller groups, [Telonemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telonemia "Telonemia"), [Haptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptista "Haptista") and [Cryptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptista "Cryptista"), also belong to Diaphoretickes.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)[TSAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAR_supergroup#Internal_phylogeny "SAR supergroup") is a possible clade that would comprise Telonemia and SAR,[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-60) although Telonemia may branch with Haptista instead of SAR.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-61)[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-62) Telonemia shares some cellular similarities with the SAR supergroup.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tikhonenkov-2022b-59)

The stramenopiles, also known as Heterokonta, are characterized by the presence of two cilia, one of which bears many short, straw-like hairs ([mastigonemes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mastigoneme "Mastigoneme")). They include one clade of phototrophs and numerous clades of heterotrophs, present in virtually all habitats. Stramenopiles include two usually well-supported clades, [Bigyra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bigyra "Bigyra") and [Gyrista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gyrista "Gyrista"), although the [monophyly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monophyly "Monophyly") of Bigyra is being questioned.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Jirsov%C3%A1-2024-63) Branching outside both Bigyra and Gyrista is a single species of enigmatic heterotrophic flagellates, _[Platysulcus tardus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platysulcus\_tardus "Platysulcus tardus")_.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Jirsov%C3%A1-2024-63) Much of the diversity of heterotrophic stramenopiles is still uncharacterized, known almost entirely from lineages of genetic sequences known as MASTs (MArine STramenopiles),[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Jirsov%C3%A1-2024-63) of which only a few species have been described.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-64)[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-65)

The phylum Gyrista includes the photosynthetic [Ochrophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ochrophyta "Ochrophyta") or Heterokontophyta (>23,000 species),[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) which contain chloroplasts originated from a [red alga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_alga "Red alga"). Among these are many lineages of algae that encompass a wide range of structures and morphologies. The three most diverse ochrophyte classes are: the [diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatom "Diatom"), unicellular or colonial organisms encased in silica cell walls ([frustules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frustule "Frustule")) that exhibit widely different shapes and ornamentations and comprise much of the [marine phytoplankton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marine_phytoplankton "Marine phytoplankton");[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Mann-2017-66) the [brown algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_algae "Brown algae"), filamentous or 'truly' multicellular (with differentiated tissues) macroalgae that constitute the basis of many temperate and cold marine ecosystems, such as [kelp forests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelp_forest "Kelp forest");[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Kawai-2017-67) and the [golden algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_algae "Golden algae"), unicellular or colonial flagellates that are mostly present in freshwater habitats.[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Kristiansen-2017-68) Inside Gyrista, the sister clade to Ochrophyta are the predominantly [osmotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmotroph "Osmotroph") and filamentous [pseudofungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudofungi "Pseudofungi") (>1,200 species),[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Thines-2018-69) which include three distinct lineages: the parasitic [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycetes "Oomycetes") or water moulds (e.g., _[Phytophthora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytophthora "Phytophthora")_), which encompass most of the pseudofungi species; the less diverse non-parasitic [hyphochytrids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyphochytrid "Hyphochytrid") that maintain a fungus-like lifestyle; and the [bigyromonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bigyromonad "Bigyromonad"), a group of bacterivorous or eukaryovorous phagotrophs.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Jirsov%C3%A1-2024-63) A small group of heliozoan-like heterotrophic amoebae, [Actinophryida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actinophryida "Actinophryida"), has an uncertain position, either within or as the sister taxon of Ochrophyta.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Azuma-2022-70)

The little studied phylum Bigyra is an assemblage of exclusively heterotrophic organisms, most of which are free-living. It includes the [labyrinthulomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labyrinthulomycetes "Labyrinthulomycetes"), among which are single-celled amoeboid phagotrophs, mixotrophs, and fungus-like filamentous heterotrophs that create slime networks to move and absorb nutrients, as well as some parasites and a few testate amoebae ([Amphitremida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphitremida "Amphitremida")). Also included in Bigyra are the [bicosoecids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicosoecid "Bicosoecid"), phagotrophic flagellates that consume bacteria, and the closely related [Placidozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placidozoa "Placidozoa"), which consists of several groups of heterotrophic flagellates (e.g., the deep-sea halophilic [Placididea](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Placididea&action=edit&redlink=1 "Placididea (page does not exist)")) as well as the intestinal [commensals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commensal "Commensal") known as [Opalinata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opalinata "Opalinata") (e.g., the human parasite _[Blastocystis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastocystis "Blastocystis")_, and the highly unusual [opalinids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opalinid "Opalinid"), composed of giant cells with numerous nuclei and cilia, originally misclassified as ciliates).[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Jirsov%C3%A1-2024-63)

*   [![Image 10: Phytophthora, the oomycete genus that includes the potato blight behind the Great Famine of Ireland](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Zoospore_release.jpg/120px-Zoospore_release.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Zoospore_release.jpg "Phytophthora, the oomycete genus that includes the potato blight behind the Great Famine of Ireland")

*   [![Image 11: Diatoms are responsible for a big portion of the oxygen produced worldwide](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Diatom3.jpg/120px-Diatom3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Diatom3.jpg "Diatoms are responsible for a big portion of the oxygen produced worldwide")

[Diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatom "Diatom") are responsible for a big portion of the [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen "Oxygen") produced worldwide

*   [![Image 12: Macrocystis pyrifera, the giant kelp](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Giant_kelp_%28Macrocystis_pyrifera%29_holdfast.jpg/120px-Giant_kelp_%28Macrocystis_pyrifera%29_holdfast.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Giant_kelp_(Macrocystis_pyrifera)_holdfast.jpg "Macrocystis pyrifera, the giant kelp")

*   [![Image 13: Cafeteria, a genus of bicosoecids](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Cafeteria_roenbergensis_atcc50561_Protsville.jpg/120px-Cafeteria_roenbergensis_atcc50561_Protsville.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cafeteria_roenbergensis_atcc50561_Protsville.jpg "Cafeteria, a genus of bicosoecids")

_[Cafeteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cafeteria\_(bicosoecid) "Cafeteria (bicosoecid)")_, a genus of bicosoecids 
*   [![Image 14: Opalina cell covered in numerous rows of cilia](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Opalina_ranarum_Protsville.jpg/120px-Opalina_ranarum_Protsville.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Opalina_ranarum_Protsville.jpg "Opalina cell covered in numerous rows of cilia")

_[Opalina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opalina "Opalina")_ cell covered in numerous rows of cilia

The [alveolates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alveolate "Alveolate") (Alveolata) are characterized by the presence of [cortical alveoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cortical_alveoli "Cortical alveoli"), cytoplasmic sacs underlying the [cell membrane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_membrane "Cell membrane") of unknown physiological function.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Madigan-2019-45): 599  Among them are three of the most well-known groups of protists: apicomplexans, dinoflagellates and ciliates. The ciliates ([Ciliophora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliophora "Ciliophora")) are a highly diverse (>8,000 species) and probably the most thoroughly studied[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) group of protists. They are mostly free-living microbes characterized by large cells covered in rows of cilia and containing two kinds of nuclei, micronucleus and macronucleus. Free-living ciliates are usually the top heterotrophs and predators in microbial food webs, feeding on bacteria and smaller eukaryotes, present in a variety of ecosystems, although a few species are [kleptoplastic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kleptoplastic "Kleptoplastic"). Others are parasitic of numerous animals.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lynn-2017-71) Ciliates have a basal position in the evolution of alveolates, together with a few species of heterotrophic flagellates with two cilia collectively known as [colponemids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colponemid "Colponemid").[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Janou%C5%A1kovec-2013-72)

The remaining alveolates are grouped under the clade [Myzozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myzozoa "Myzozoa"), whose common ancestor acquired chloroplasts through a secondary endosymbiosis from a red alga.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Janou%C5%A1kovec-2015-73) One branch of Myzozoa contains the apicomplexans and their closest relatives, a small clade of flagellates known as [Chrompodellida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrompodellida "Chrompodellida") where phototrophic and heterotrophic flagellates, called [chromerids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromerid "Chromerid") and [colpodellids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colpodellid "Colpodellid") respectively, are evolutionarily intermingled.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Janou%C5%A1kovec-2015-73) In contrast, the apicomplexans ([Apicomplexa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa")) are a large (>6,000 species) and highly specialized group of obligate parasites who have all secondarily lost their photosynthetic ability (e.g., _[Plasmodium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmodium "Plasmodium")_). Their adult stages absorb nutrients from the host through the cell membrane, and they reproduce between hosts via sporozoites, which exhibit an [organelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organelle "Organelle") complex (the [apicoplast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicoplast "Apicoplast")) evolved from non-photosynthetic chloroplasts.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Vot%C3%BDpka-2017-74)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Madigan-2019-45): 600

The other branch of Myzozoa contains the dinoflagellates and their closest relatives, the perkinsids ([Perkinsozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perkinsozoa "Perkinsozoa")), a small group (26 species) of aquatic intracellular parasites which have lost their photosynthetic ability similarly to apicomplexans.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Janou%C5%A1kovec-2015-73) They reproduce through flagellated spores that infect dinoflagellates, [molluscs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mollusc "Mollusc") and [fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish "Fish").[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-75) In contrast, the dinoflagellates ([Dinoflagellata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellata "Dinoflagellata")) are a highly diversified (~4,500 species)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Saldarriaga-2017-76) group of aquatic algae that have mostly retained their chloroplasts, although many lineages have lost their own and instead either live as heterotrophs or reacquire new chloroplasts from other sources, including tertiary endosymbiosis and [kleptoplasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kleptoplasty "Kleptoplasty").[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-77) Most dinoflagellates are free-living and compose an important portion of phytoplankton, as well as a major cause of [harmful algal blooms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmful_algal_bloom "Harmful algal bloom") due to their toxicity; some live as symbionts of corals, allowing the creation of coral reefs. Dinoflagellates exhibit a diversity of cellular structures, such as complex eyelike ocelli, specialized vacuoles, bioluminescent organelles, and a wall surrounding the cell known as the [theca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theca "Theca").[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Saldarriaga-2017-76)

*   [![Image 15: Paramecium, a well-studied genus of ciliates[74]](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/%D0%98%D0%BD%D1%84%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D1%82%D1%83%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B0_2.tif/lossy-page1-110px-%D0%98%D0%BD%D1%84%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D1%82%D1%83%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B0_2.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%98%D0%BD%D1%84%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D1%82%D1%83%D1%84%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B0_2.tif "Paramecium, a well-studied genus of ciliates[74]")

_[Paramecium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramecium "Paramecium")_, a well-studied genus of ciliates[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-78)

*   [![Image 18: Dinovorax, a perkinsid that infects dinoflagellates](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dinovorax_pyriformis_PMC5609580_fig1c.png/120px-Dinovorax_pyriformis_PMC5609580_fig1c.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dinovorax_pyriformis_PMC5609580_fig1c.png "Dinovorax, a perkinsid that infects dinoflagellates")

_[Dinovorax](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dinovorax&action=edit&redlink=1 "Dinovorax (page does not exist)")_, a perkinsid that infects dinoflagellates

*   [![Image 19: Alexandrium dinoflagellates, responsible for certain harmful algal blooms](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alexandrium_catenella.jpg/120px-Alexandrium_catenella.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alexandrium_catenella.jpg "Alexandrium dinoflagellates, responsible for certain harmful algal blooms")

_[Alexandrium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandrium\_(dinoflagellate) "Alexandrium (dinoflagellate)")_ dinoflagellates, responsible for certain harmful algal blooms

[Rhizaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizaria "Rhizaria") is a lineage of morphologically diverse organisms, composed almost entirely of unicellular heterotrophic amoebae, flagellates and amoeboflagellates,[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) commonly with reticulose (net-like) or filose (thread-like) [pseudopodia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudopodia "Pseudopodia") for feeding and locomotion.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2018-79)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Madigan-2019-45): 604  It was the last supergroup to be described, because it lacks any [defining characteristic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synapomorphy "Synapomorphy") and was discovered exclusively through [molecular phylogenetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_phylogenetics "Molecular phylogenetics").[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Burki-2014-80) Three major clades are included, namely the phyla [Cercozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cercozoa "Cercozoa"), [Endomyxa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endomyxa "Endomyxa") and [Retaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retaria "Retaria").[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)

Retaria contains the most familiar rhizarians: [forams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foram "Foram") and [radiolarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria"), two groups of large free-living marine amoebae with pseudopodia supported by [microtubules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microtubule "Microtubule"), many of which are macroscopic.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) The radiolarians (Radiolaria) are a diverse group (>1,000 living species) of amoebae, often bearing delicate and intricate siliceous skeletons.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Biard-2022-81) The forams (Foraminifera) are also diverse (>6,700 living species),[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2014-82) and most of them are encased in multichambered tests constructed from calcium carbonate or agglutinated mineral particles.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Both groups have a rich fossil record, with tens of thousands of described fossil species.[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2014-82)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Boltovskoy-2017-83)

Cercozoa (also known as [Filosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filosa "Filosa")) is an assemblage of free-living protists with very different morphologies. Cercozoan amoeboflagellates are important predators of other microbes in terrestrial habitats and the plant microbiota (e.g., [cercomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cercomonad "Cercomonad") and [paracercomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paracercomonad "Paracercomonad") and [glissomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glissomonad "Glissomonad"), collectively known as class [SARcomonadea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarcomonadea "Sarcomonadea")),[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Dumack-2017-84) and a few can generate slime molds (e.g., [Helkesea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helkesea "Helkesea")).[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-85) Many cercozoans are testate or scale-bearing amoebae, namely the elusive _[Kraken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kraken\_(genus) "Kraken (genus)")_ and the two classes [Imbricatea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imbricatea "Imbricatea") (e.g., the [euglyphids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglyphid "Euglyphid")) and [Thecofilosea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thecofilosea "Thecofilosea").[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Dumack-2017-84) Thecofilosea also contains the [Phaeodaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phaeodaria "Phaeodaria") (~400â€“500 species), a group of skeleton-bearing marine amoebae previously classified as radiolarians,[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Boltovskoy-2017-83) and both classes include some non-scaly naked flagellates (e.g., [spongomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spongomonad "Spongomonad") in Imbricatea and [thaumatomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thaumatomonad "Thaumatomonad") in Thecofilosea).[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Howe-2011-86) Among the basal-branching cercozoans are the pseudopodia-lacking thecate flagellates of [Metromonadea](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Metromonadea&action=edit&redlink=1 "Metromonadea (page does not exist)"), the heliozoan-like [Granofilosea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Granofilosea "Granofilosea")[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Howe-2011-86) and the photosynthetic [chlorarachniophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorarachniophyte "Chlorarachniophyte"), whose chloroplasts originated from a secondary endosymbiosis with a green alga.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18)

Endomyxa contains two major clades of parasitic protists: [Ascetosporea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ascetosporea "Ascetosporea") are sporozoan-type parasites of marine invertebrates,[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-87) while [Phytomyxea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytomyxea "Phytomyxea") are obligate pathogens of plants and algae, divided into the terrestrial [plasmodiophorids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmodiophorid "Plasmodiophorid") and the marine [phagomyxids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagomyxid "Phagomyxid").[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-88) Also included in Endomyxa are the order of predatory amoebae [Vampyrellida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampyrellida "Vampyrellida") (48 species)[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hess-2022-89) and two genera of marine amoebae, the thecate _[Gromia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gromia "Gromia")_ and the naked _[Filoreta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filoreta "Filoreta")_.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)

Besides these three phyla, Rhizaria includes numerous enigmatic and understudied lineages of uncertain evolutionary position. One such clade is the [Gymnosphaerida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gymnosphaerida "Gymnosphaerida"), which includes heliozoan-type protists.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gast-2017-90) Several clades labeled as Novel Clades (NC) are entirely composed of [environmental DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA") from uncultured protists, although a few have slowly been resolved over the decades with the description of new taxa (e.g., [Tremulida](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tremulida&action=edit&redlink=1 "Tremulida (page does not exist)") and [Aquavolonida](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aquavolonida&action=edit&redlink=1 "Aquavolonida (page does not exist)"), formerly NC11 and NC10 respectively, with a deep-branching position in Rhizaria).[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Bass-2018-91)

#### Haptista and Cryptista

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Haptista and Cryptista")]

[Haptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptista "Haptista") and [Cryptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptista "Cryptista") are two similar phyla of single-celled protists previously thought to be closely related, and collectively known as [Hacrobia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hacrobia "Hacrobia").[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2015-92) However, the monophyly of Hacrobia was disproven, as the two groups originated independently.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-93) Molecular analyses place Cryptista next to Archaeplastida, forming the hypothesized [CAM clade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CAM_clade "CAM clade"),[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yazaki-2022-42) and Haptista next to the Telonemia and the SAR clade[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eglit-2024-43) (Telonemia may either be the sister group to SAR, forming the hypothesized TSAR clade,[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Burki-2020-94) or to Haptista, forming a common sister clade to SAR[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Torruella-2025-95)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yazaki-2022-42)[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Williamson-2025-96)). Within the CAM clade, the closest relative of Cryptista is the species _[Microheliella maris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microheliella\_maris "Microheliella maris")_, together composing the clade [Pancryptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pancryptista "Pancryptista").[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yazaki-2022-42)

The phylum Haptista includes two distinct clades with mineralized scales: [haptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptophyte "Haptophyte") and [centrohelids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrohelid "Centrohelid").[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) The haptophytes (Haptophyta) are a group of over 500 living species[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) of flagellated or coccoid algae that have acquired chloroplasts from a secondary endosymbiosis. They are mostly marine, comprise an important portion of oceanic plankton, and include the [coccolithophores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coccolithophore "Coccolithophore"), whose calcified scales ('[coccoliths](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coccolith "Coccolith")') contribute to the formation of sedimentary rocks and the biogeochemical cycles of carbon and calcium. Some species are capable of forming toxic blooms.[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eikrem-2017-97) The centrohelids (Centroplasthelida) are a small (~95 species)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2007-98) but widespread group of heterotrophic heliozoan-type amoebae, usually covered in scale-bearing mucous, that form an important component of benthic food webs of aquatic habitats, both marine and freshwater.[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Zagumyonnyi-2022-99)

The phylum Cryptista is a clade of three distinct groups of unicellular protists: [cryptomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptomonad "Cryptomonad"), [katablepharids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katablepharid "Katablepharid"), and the species _[Palpitomonas bilix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palpitomonas\_bilix "Palpitomonas bilix")_.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) The cryptomonads (>100 species), also known as cryptophytes, are flagellated algae found in aquatic habitats of diverse salinity, characterized by extrusive organelles or [extrusomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extrusome "Extrusome") called ejectisomes. Their chloroplasts, of red algal origin, contain a [nucleomorph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleomorph "Nucleomorph"), a remnant of the eukaryotic nucleus belonging to the endosymbiotic red alga.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hoef-Emden-2017-100) The katablepharids, the closest relatives of cryptomonads, are heterotrophic flagellates with two cilia, also characterized by ejectisomes.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2015-92)[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) The species _Palpitomonas bilix_ is the most basal-branching member of Cryptista, a marine heterotrophic flagellate with two cilia, but unlike the remaining members it lacks ejectisomes.[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-101)

*   [![Image 25: Raphidiophrys, a centrohelid heliozoan](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Raphidiophrys_contractilis.jpg/120px-Raphidiophrys_contractilis.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Raphidiophrys_contractilis.jpg "Raphidiophrys, a centrohelid heliozoan")

_[Raphidiophrys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raphidiophrys "Raphidiophrys")_, a centrohelid heliozoan 
*   [![Image 26: Coccolithophore covered in coccoliths](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Coccolithus-pelagicus_hg.jpg/120px-Coccolithus-pelagicus_hg.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Coccolithus-pelagicus_hg.jpg "Coccolithophore covered in coccoliths")

[Coccolithophore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coccolithophore "Coccolithophore") covered in coccoliths 
*   [![Image 27: Cryptomonas, common algae in fresh waters worldwide](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cryptomonas_platyuris_-_160x_%2813286242253%29.jpg/120px-Cryptomonas_platyuris_-_160x_%2813286242253%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cryptomonas_platyuris_-_160x_(13286242253).jpg "Cryptomonas, common algae in fresh waters worldwide")

_[Cryptomonas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptomonas "Cryptomonas")_, common algae in fresh waters worldwide

*   [![Image 28: Roombia truncata, filled with rows of ejectisomes](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Roombia_truncata_cells-fig-a.tif/lossy-page1-101px-Roombia_truncata_cells-fig-a.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Roombia_truncata_cells-fig-a.tif "Roombia truncata, filled with rows of ejectisomes")

_[Roombia truncata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roombia\_truncata "Roombia truncata")_, filled with rows of ejectisomes 

Archaeplastida is the clade containing those photosynthetic groups whose [plastids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plastid "Plastid") were likely obtained through a single event of primary [endosymbiosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosymbiosis "Endosymbiosis") with a [cyanobacterium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanobacterium "Cyanobacterium"). It contains [land plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte") (Embryophyta) and a big portion of the diversity of algae, most of which are the [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), from which plants evolved, and the [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae").[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-De_Clerck-2012-102) A third lineage of algae, the [glaucophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glaucophyte "Glaucophyte") (25 species),[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) contains rare and obscure species found in surfaces of freshwater and terrestrial habitats.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-De_Clerck-2012-102)

The red algae or Rhodophyta (>7,100 species) are a group of diverse morphologies, ranging from single cells to [multicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellular "Multicellular") filaments to giant [pseudoparenchymatous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudoparenchyma "Pseudoparenchyma")[thalli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thalli "Thalli"), all without flagella. They lack [chlorophyll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyll "Chlorophyll") and only harvest light energy through [phycobiliproteins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phycobiliprotein "Phycobiliprotein"). Their life cycles are varied and may include two or three generations. They are present in terrestrial, freshwater and primarily marine habitats, from the intertidal zone to deep waters; some are calcified and are vital components of marine ecosystems such as [coral reefs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral_reef "Coral reef").[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yoon-2017-103) Closely related to the red algae are two small lineages of non-photosynthetic predatory flagellates: the freshwater and marine [Rhodelphidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhodelphidia "Rhodelphidia") (3 species),[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Prokina-2023-104) which still retain genetic evidence of relic plastids;[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gawryluk-2019-105) and the marine [Picozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Picozoa "Picozoa") (1 species), which lack any remains of plastids. The evolutionary position of Picozoa may indicate that there have been two separate events of primary endosymbiosis, as opposed to one.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Sch%C3%B6n-2021-106)

The green algae, unlike the [monophyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monophyly "Monophyly") glaucophytes and rhodophytes, are a [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyly "Paraphyly") group from which land plants evolved. Together they compose the [Chloroplastida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloroplastida "Chloroplastida") or Viridiplantae clade.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) The earliest branching member is the phylum [Prasinodermophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prasinodermophyta "Prasinodermophyta") (ten species), whose members are exclusively marine coccoid cells or small macroscopic thalli.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Prasinodermophyta-107) The remaining green algae are distributed in two major clades. One clade is the phylum [Chlorophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyta "Chlorophyta") (>7,900 species),[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) which includes numerous lineages of scaly unicellular flagellate algae known collectively as [prasinophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prasinophyte "Prasinophyte") along with the Prasinodermophyta, but also includes a variety of morphologies such as coccoids, palmelloids, colonies, and macroscopic filamentous, foliose or tubular thalli, present in aquatic and terrestrial habitats.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) The opposed clade is [Streptophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streptophyta "Streptophyta"), which contains the land plants and a paraphyletic group of green algae collectively known as phylum [Charophyta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charophyta "Charophyta"), composed of several classes: [Zygnematophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zygnematophyceae "Zygnematophyceae") (>4,300 species),[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) containing unicellular, colonial and filamentous flagella-lacking organisms found almost exclusively in freshwater habitats;[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hall-2017-108)[Charophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charophyceae "Charophyceae") (450 living species),[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52) also known as stoneworts, consisting of complex multicellular thalli only found in freshwater habitats;[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-McCourt-2017-109)[Klebsormidiophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klebsormidiophyceae "Klebsormidiophyceae") (52 species), with unbranched filamentous thalli; [Coleochaetophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coleochaetophyceae "Coleochaetophyceae") (36 species), containing branched filamentous thalli; [Mesostigmatophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesostigmatophyceae "Mesostigmatophyceae"), composed of a single species of scaly flagellates; and [Chlorokybophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorokybophyceae "Chlorokybophyceae") (five species), with sarcinoid forms.[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cook-2017-110)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Guiry-2024-52)

*   [![Image 29: Cyanophora, a glaucophyte genus](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Woelfib_cyanphoraparadoxa_0632002_img_8087093_2979_sag005_20131025205735_small.jpg/120px-Woelfib_cyanphoraparadoxa_0632002_img_8087093_2979_sag005_20131025205735_small.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Woelfib_cyanphoraparadoxa_0632002_img_8087093_2979_sag005_20131025205735_small.jpg "Cyanophora, a glaucophyte genus")

_[Cyanophora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanophora "Cyanophora")_, a glaucophyte genus 
*   [![Image 30: Corallina officinalis, a coralline red alga](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Corallina_officinalis_at_Kakamatua_Point%2C_Huia.jpg/120px-Corallina_officinalis_at_Kakamatua_Point%2C_Huia.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Corallina_officinalis_at_Kakamatua_Point,_Huia.jpg "Corallina officinalis, a coralline red alga")

_[Corallina officinalis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corallina\_officinalis "Corallina officinalis")_, a coralline red alga 
*   [![Image 31: Volvox, a colonial chlorophyte](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Volvox_aureus.jpg/120px-Volvox_aureus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Volvox_aureus.jpg "Volvox, a colonial chlorophyte")

_[Volvox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvox "Volvox")_, a colonial chlorophyte

*   [![Image 32: Spirogyra, a filamentous streptophyte, during conjugation](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Spirogyra_3.jpg/120px-Spirogyra_3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Spirogyra_3.jpg "Spirogyra, a filamentous streptophyte, during conjugation")

_[Spirogyra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirogyra "Spirogyra")_, a filamentous streptophyte, during [conjugation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_conjugation "Sexual conjugation") 
*   [![Image 33: Chara, a complex plant-like streptophyte with reproductive structures](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Chara_sp_reproductive_structure.JPG/120px-Chara_sp_reproductive_structure.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Chara_sp_reproductive_structure.JPG "Chara, a complex plant-like streptophyte with reproductive structures")

_[Chara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chara\_(alga) "Chara (alga)")_, a complex plant-like streptophyte with reproductive structures

[Amorphea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amorphea "Amorphea") is a group of exclusively heterotrophic organisms. It contains the fungi and animals, as well as most slime moulds, many amoebae and some flagellates.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Heiss-2018-111) Many of its protist members exhibit complex life cycles with different levels of multicellularity.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lam%C5%BCa-2023-112) Amorphea is roughly equivalent to the concept of 'unikonts', meaning 'single cilium', although it currently contains several organisms with more cilia.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2013-113) It is defined as the smallest clade containing the groups [Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa") (containing mostly slime moulds and amoebae) and [Opisthokonta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthokonta "Opisthokonta") (containing fungi, animals, and their closest relatives).[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Heiss-2018-111)[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) The closest relatives of Opisthokonta are two small lineages of single-celled protists with two cilia: the flagellate [Apusomonadida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apusomonadida "Apusomonadida") (28 species)[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Torruella-2022-114) and the amoeboflagellate anaerobic [Breviatea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breviatea "Breviatea") (four species).[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Together with opisthokonts, these two groups form the clade [Obazoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obazoa "Obazoa"), the sister clade to Amoebozoa.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2013-113)

The phylum [Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa") (2,400 species)[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2012-36) is a large group of morphologically diverse phagotrophic protists, mostly amoebae. A considerable portion of amoebozoans are [lobose amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobosa "Lobosa"), meaning they produce round, blunt-ended pseudopods.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Smirnov-2005-115) It includes the 'archetypal' amoebae, known as the naked lobose amoebae or 'gymnamoebae'[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Page-1987-116) (such as _[Amoeba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoeba\_(genus) "Amoeba (genus)")_ itself),[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tekle-2022-117) among which is a genus of sorocarp-forming slime moulds, _[Copromyxa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copromyxa "Copromyxa")_.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2010a-118) Some gymnamoebae are important pathogens to animals (e.g., _[Acanthamoeba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acanthamoeba "Acanthamoeba")_).[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-119) Other relevant lobose amoebae are the [Arcellinida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arcellinida "Arcellinida"), a diverse order of testate amoebae and one of the most conspicuous protist groups overall.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gonz%C3%A1lez-Migu%C3%A9ns-2022-120) The remaining, non-lobose amoebozoans include the [Eumycetozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eumycetozoa "Eumycetozoa") or 'true slime moulds', comprising the sorocarp-producing bacterivorous [dictyostelids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dictyostelid "Dictyostelid") and the sporocarp-producing omnivorous [myxogastrids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxogastrid "Myxogastrid") and [protosporangiids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protosporangiida "Protosporangiida").[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) Due to the fungus-like appearance of their fruiting bodies, eumycetozoans are often studied by mycologists.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) Closely related to the eumycetozoans are two lineages: the [Variosea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variosea "Variosea"), a heterogeneous assortment of amoeboid, reticulate or flagellated organisms[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tekle-2022-117) (including some sorocarp-producing organisms);[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Berney-2015-121) and the anaerobic [Archamoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archamoebae "Archamoebae"), some of which live as intestinal symbionts of some animals (e.g., _[Entamoeba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entamoeba "Entamoeba")_).[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)

Opisthokonta includes the animal and fungal kingdoms,[[a]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-kingdoms-13) as well as their closest protist relatives. The branch leading to the fungi is known as [Nucletmycea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucletmycea "Nucletmycea") or Holomycota, while the branch leading to the animals is called [Holozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holozoa "Holozoa").[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Galindo-2021-122) The Holomycota includes the closest relatives of fungi, the [nucleariids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleariid "Nucleariid"), a small group (~50 species) of free-living naked or scale-bearing phagotrophic amoebae with filose pseudopodia, some of which can aggregate into slime moulds.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gabald%C3%B3n-2022-123) Within the wider definition of fungi, three groups are studied as protists by some authors: [Aphelida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphelida "Aphelida") (15 species),[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wijayawardene-2022-12)[Rozellida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rozellida "Rozellida") (27 species)[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lechter-2018-124) and [Microsporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsporidia "Microsporidia") (~1,300 species),[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cali-2017-125) collectively known as [Opisthosporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthosporidia "Opisthosporidia"), as opposed to the 'true' or osmotrophic fungi. Both aphelids and rozellids are single-celled phagotrophic flagellates that feed in an endobiotic manner, penetrating the cells of their respective hosts. Microsporidians are obligate intracellular parasites that feed through osmotrophy, much like true fungi. Aphelids and true fungi are closest relatives, and generally feed on cellulose-walled organisms (many algae and plants). Conversely, rozellids and microsporidians form a separate clade, and generally feed on chitin-walled organisms (fungi and animals).[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Galindo-2022-126)

The Holozoa includes various lineages with complex life cycles involving different cell types and associated with the origin of animal multicellularity.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Simpson-2017a-18) The closest relatives to animals are the [choanoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choanoflagellate "Choanoflagellate") (~360 species), free-living flagellates that feed through a collar of microvilli surrounding a larger cilium and often form colonies.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Richter-2017-127) The [Ichthyosporea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ichthyosporea "Ichthyosporea") (>40 species), otherwise known as mesomycetozoans, are a group of fungus-like pathogenic holozoans specialized in infecting fish and other animals.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Glockling-2013-128) The [Filasterea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filasterea "Filasterea") (six species) are a heterogeneous group of free-living, endosymbiotic, or parasitic amoebae or flagellates.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-129) Lastly, the [Pluriformea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluriformea "Pluriformea") are two species of free-living holozoans with life cycles that include multicellular aggregates.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hehenberger-2017-130) An elusive flagellate species _[Tunicaraptor unikontum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunicaraptor\_unikontum "Tunicaraptor unikontum")_ has an uncertain evolutionary position among these holozoan groups.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tikhonenkov-2020-131)

*   [![Image 34: Amoeba, the archetypal amoebae](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Amoeba.png/120px-Amoeba.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Amoeba.png "Amoeba, the archetypal amoebae")

_[Amoeba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoeba\_(genus) "Amoeba (genus)")_, the archetypal amoebae

*   [![Image 35: Physarum polycephalum, a true slime mould](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/American_physarum_polycephalum_2.jpg/120px-American_physarum_polycephalum_2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:American_physarum_polycephalum_2.jpg "Physarum polycephalum, a true slime mould")

*   [![Image 36: Nuclearia, filose amoebae related to fungi](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Nuclearia_sp_Nikko.jpg/120px-Nuclearia_sp_Nikko.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nuclearia_sp_Nikko.jpg "Nuclearia, filose amoebae related to fungi")

_[Nuclearia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclearia "Nuclearia")_, filose amoebae related to fungi

*   [![Image 37: Creolimax fragrantissima, an ichthyosporean that infects peanut worms](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Creolimax_fragrantissima.jpg/120px-Creolimax_fragrantissima.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Creolimax_fragrantissima.jpg "Creolimax fragrantissima, an ichthyosporean that infects peanut worms")

*   [![Image 38: A choanoflagellate colony, with cells resembling choanocytes found in sponges](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/PhysRevLett.116.038102-Fig1a.jpg/120px-PhysRevLett.116.038102-Fig1a.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PhysRevLett.116.038102-Fig1a.jpg "A choanoflagellate colony, with cells resembling choanocytes found in sponges")

A choanoflagellate colony, with cells resembling [choanocytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choanocyte "Choanocyte") found in [sponges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sponge "Sponge")
