Several smaller lineages do not belong to any of the three main supergroups, and instead have a deep-branching "kingdom-level" position in eukaryote evolution. They are usually poorly known groups with limited data and few species, often referred to as "orphan groups".[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eglit-2024-43) The [CRuMs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CRuMs "CRuMs") clade, containing the free-swimming [Collodictyonidae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collodictyonidae "Collodictyonidae") (seven species) with two to four cilia, the amoeboid [Rigifilida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigifilida "Rigifilida") (two species) with filose pseudopodia, and the gliding [Mantamonadidae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantamonadidae "Mantamonadidae") (three species)[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Blaz-2021-132) and [Glissandridae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glissandridae "Glissandridae") (two species)[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yazaki-2025-133)[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Patterson_1996-134) with two cilia, are the sister clade of Amorphea.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2018-41) The [Ancyromonadida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancyromonadida "Ancyromonadida") (35 species)[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Yubuki_2023-135) are aquatic gliding flagellates with two cilia, positioned near Amorphea and CRuMs.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2018-41) The [Hemimastigophora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemimastigophora "Hemimastigophora") (ten species), or hemimastigotes, are predatory flagellates with a distinctive cell morphology and two rows of around a dozen flagella.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lax-2018-136) The [Provora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provora "Provora") (eight species)[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Belyaev-2024-137) are predatory flagellates with an unremarkable morphology similar to that of excavates and other flagellates with two cilia. Both Hemimastigophora and Provora were thought to be related to or within Diaphoretickes,[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tikhonenkov-2022a-3) although further analyses have placed them in a separate clade along with a mysterious species of predatory protists, _[Meteora sporadica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteora\_sporadica "Meteora sporadica")_. This species has a remarkable morphology: they lack flagella, are bilaterally symmetrical, project a pair of lateral "arms" that swing back and forth, and contain a system of motility unlike any other.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Eglit-2024-43)

There are also many [genera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genera "Genera") of uncertain affiliation among eukaryotes because their DNA has not been [sequenced](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_sequencing "DNA sequencing"), and consequently their phylogenetic affinities are unknown.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) One enigmatic heliozoan species is so large that it does not match the description of any known genus, and was consequently transferred to a separate genus _[Berkeleyaesol](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berkeleyaesol&action=edit&redlink=1 "Berkeleyaesol (page does not exist)")_ with an unclear position, although it probably belongs to Diaphoretickes along with all other heliozoa.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Shishkin-2021-138) The organism _[Parakaryon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parakaryon "Parakaryon")_ is harder to place, as it shares traits from both prokaryotes and eukaryotes.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-yamaguchi-139)

In general, protists have typical [eukaryotic cells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic_cell "Eukaryotic cell") that follow the same principles of [biology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology "Biology") described for those cells within the "higher" eukaryotes (animals, fungi and land plants).[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-140) However, many have evolved a variety of unique physiological adaptations that do not appear in the remaining eukaryotes,[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levandowsky-2012-141) and in fact protists encompass almost all of the broad spectrum of [biological characteristics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_trait "Biological trait") expected in eukaryotes.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Burki-2021-40)

Protists display a wide variety of food preferences and feeding mechanisms.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142) According to the source of their nutrients, they can be divided into _[autotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autotroph "Autotroph")_ (producers, traditionally [algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae "Algae")) and _[heterotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotroph "Heterotroph")_ (consumers, traditionally [protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa")). Autotrophic protists [synthesize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosynthesis "Biosynthesis") their own organic compounds from inorganic substrates through the process of [photosynthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthesis "Photosynthesis"), using light as the source of energy;[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hickman-2017-143): 217  accordingly, they are also known as _[phototrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phototroph "Phototroph")_.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lwoff-1946-144)

Heterotrophic protists obtain organic molecules synthesized by other organisms, and can be further divided according to the size of their nutrients. Those that feed on soluble molecules[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hickman-2017-143): 218  or macromolecules under 0.5 Î¼m in size are called _[osmotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmotroph "Osmotroph")_,[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142) and they absorb them by [diffusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diffusion "Diffusion"), ciliary pits, [transport proteins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transport_protein "Transport protein") of the cell membrane, and a type of [endocytosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocytosis "Endocytosis") (i.e., invagination of the cell membrane into [vacuoles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuole "Vacuole"), called [endosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosome "Endosome")) known as [pinocytosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinocytosis "Pinocytosis")[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) or fluid-phase endocytosis.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142) Those that feed on organic particles over 0.5 Î¼m in size or entire cells are called _[phagotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagotroph "Phagotroph")_, and they ingest them through a type of endocytosis known as [phagocytosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagocytosis "Phagocytosis").[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142)[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hickman-2017-143): 218  Endocytosis is considered one of the most important [adaptations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_adaptation "Evolutionary adaptation") in the origin of eukaryotes because it increased the potential food supply, and phagocytosis allowed the [endosymbiosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosymbiosis "Endosymbiosis") and development of [mitochondria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondria "Mitochondria") and [chloroplasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloroplast "Chloroplast"). In both osmotrophs and phagotrophs, endocytosis is often restricted to a specific region of the cell membrane, known as the [cytostome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytostome "Cytostome"), which may be followed by a cytopharynx, a specialized tract supported by [microtubules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microtubule "Microtubule").[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142)

Osmotrophic protists acquire soluble nutrients through [membrane channels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Membrane_channel "Membrane channel") and [carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Membrane_carrier "Membrane carrier"), but also through different types of pinocytosis. Macropinocytosis involves the folding of membrane into ruffles,[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-145) which creates large (0.2 to 1.0 Î¼m) vacuoles. Micropinocytosis involves smaller vesicles that are usually formed by [clathrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clathrin "Clathrin"). In both scenarios, the vesicles merge into a digestive vacuole or [endosome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosome "Endosome") where digestion takes place.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142) Some osmotrophs, called _[saprotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saprotroph "Saprotroph")_ or _lysotrophs_, perform external digestion by releasing enzymes into the environment and decomposing organic matter[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) into simpler molecules that can be absorbed. This external digestion has a distinct advantage: it allows greater control over the substances that are allowed to enter the cell, thus minimizing the intake of harmful substances or infection.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Richards-2013-146)

Probably all eukaryotes are capable of osmotrophy, but some have no alternative of acquiring nutrients. Obligate osmotrophs and saprotrophs include some [euglenids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenid "Euglenid"), some [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), the human parasite _[Blastocystis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastocystis "Blastocystis")_, some [metamonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamonad "Metamonad"),[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) the parasitic [trypanosomatids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trypanosomatid "Trypanosomatid"),[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-147) and the fungus-like [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycetes "Oomycetes") and [hyphochytrids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyphochytrid "Hyphochytrid").[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Richards-2013-146)

[![Image 39](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Trypanosoma_cruzi_cytostome-cytopharynx_complex_structure.png/500px-Trypanosoma_cruzi_cytostome-cytopharynx_complex_structure.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trypanosoma_cruzi_cytostome-cytopharynx_complex_structure.png)

Structure of the cytostome-cytopharynx complex in _[Trypanosoma cruzi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trypanosoma\_cruzi "Trypanosoma cruzi")_. The food travels the pre-oral ridge from the flagellar pocket until it reaches the cytostome and enters the cell through the cytopharynx, where nutrients are presumably transported by [myosin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myosin "Myosin") proteins until they are enclosed in vesicles. The cytopharynx is supported by specific sets of microtubules.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-148)

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/A_sol_mit_Paramecium.jpg/250px-A_sol_mit_Paramecium.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:A_sol_mit_Paramecium.jpg)

The heliozoan _[Actinophrys sol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actinophrys "Actinophrys")_ phagocyting a _[Paramecium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramecium "Paramecium")_ ciliate

Phagotrophic feeding consists of two phases: the concentration of food particles in the environment, and the phagocytosis, which encloses the food particle in a vacuole (the [phagosome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagosome "Phagosome"))[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wiser-2024-142) where digestion takes place. In [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate") and most phagotrophic [flagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flagellate "Flagellate"), digestion occurs at the oral region or cytostome, which is covered by a single membrane from which vacuoles are formed; the phagosomes then may be shuttled to the interior of the cell along the cytopharynx.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149) In amoebae, phagocytosis takes place anywhere on the cell surface. The average food particle size is around one tenth the size of the protist cell.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Esteban-2020-150)

Phagotrophic protists can be further classified according to how they approach the nutrients. The _filter feeders_ acquire small, suspended food particles or prokaryotic cells and accumulate them by filtration into the cytostome (e.g., [choanoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choanoflagellate "Choanoflagellate"), some [chrysomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysomonad "Chrysomonad"), most ciliates);[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) filter-feeding flagellates accumulate particles by propelling them with a flagellum through a collar of rigid tentacles or pseudopodia that act as a filter, while filter-feeding ciliates generate water currents through cilia and membranelle zones surrounding the cytostome. The _raptorial feeders_ (e.g., [bicosoecids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicosoecid "Bicosoecid"), chrysomonads, [kinetoplastids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinetoplastid "Kinetoplastid"), some euglenids, many [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate") and ciliates), instead of retaining all particles in bulk, capture each particle individually.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Esteban-2020-150) Among raptorial protists, the _grazers_ search and ingest prey from surfaces covered with potential food items such as [bacterial lawns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterial_lawn "Bacterial lawn"), while the _[predators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predation "Predation")_ actively pursue scarce prey.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) Predators that feed on filamentous algae or fungal [hyphae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyphae "Hyphae") either swallow the filaments entirely or penetrate the cell wall and ingest the [cytoplasm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoplasm "Cytoplasm") (e.g., [Viridiraptoridae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viridiraptoridae "Viridiraptoridae")).[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2) Predators may have adaptations to hunt prey, such as 'toxicysts' that immobilize prey cells. Certain ciliates have developed a specialized kind of raptorial feeding called _histophagy_, where they attack damaged but live animals (e.g., annelids and small crustaceans), enter the wounds, and ingest animal tissue. Large raptorial amoebae enclose their prey in a "food cup" of pseudopodia, prior to the formation of the food vacuole.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Esteban-2020-150) Lastly, _diffusion feeders_ (e.g., [heliozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliozoa "Heliozoa"), [foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") and many other amoebae, [suctorian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suctoria "Suctoria") ciliates) engulf prey that happen to collide with their pseudopods or, in the case of ciliates, tentacles that carry toxicysts or extrusomes to immobilize the prey.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Esteban-2020-150)

Consumers of prokaryotes are popularly called _[bacterivores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterivore "Bacterivore")_ (e.g., most amoebae), while consumers (including osmotrophic parasites) of eukaryotes are known as _eukaryovores_. In particular, eukaryovores that feed on unicellular protists are _cytotrophs_ (e.g., [colponemids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colponemid "Colponemid"), [colpodellids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colpodellid "Colpodellid"), many amoebae, some ciliates); those that feed on fungi are _mycophages_ or _mycotrophs_ (e.g., the ciliate family [Grossglockneriidae](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Grossglockneriidae&action=edit&redlink=1 "Grossglockneriidae (page does not exist)") of obligate mycophages);[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2016-151) those that prey on [nematodes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nematode "Nematode") are _nematophages_;[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2015-152) and those that feed on algae are _phycotrophs_ (e.g., [vampyrellids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampyrellid "Vampyrellid")).[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1e.webp/120px-Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1e.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1e.webp)

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1f.webp/120px-Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1f.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1f.webp)

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1g.webp/120px-Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1g.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1g.webp)

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1h.webp/120px-Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1h.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapaza_viridis_2012_Yamaguchi_et_al_fig1h.webp)

_[Rapaza viridis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapaza\_viridis "Rapaza viridis")_ is a species of obligate specialist mixotrophs: it survives through the predation of _[Tetraselmis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tetraselmis "Tetraselmis")_ algae and acquisition of their chloroplasts. It rejects any other prey cells. Even when well fed, it cannot survive without a light source, as it needs to photosynthesize with those chloroplasts.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Karnkowska-2023-153)

Most autotrophic protists are _[mixotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixotroph "Mixotroph")_[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Sanders-2011-154) and combine photosynthesis with phagocytosis.[[e]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-156) They are classified into various functional groups or 'mixotypes'.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Mitra-2016-157)[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Faure-2019-158)_Constitutive_ mixotrophs have the innate ability to [photosynthesize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthesize "Photosynthesize") through already present chloroplasts, and have diverse feeding behaviors, as some require phototrophy, others phagotrophy, and others are obligate mixotrophs (e.g., nanoflagellates such as some [haptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptophyte "Haptophyte") and dinoflagellates). _Non-constitutive_ mixotrophs acquire the ability to photosynthesize by stealing chloroplasts from their prey, a process known as [kleptoplasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kleptoplasty "Kleptoplasty"). Non-constitutives can be divided into two: _generalists_, which can steal chloroplasts from a variety of prey (e.g., [oligotrich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligotrich "Oligotrich") ciliates), or _specialists_, which can only acquire chloroplasts from a few specific prey (e.g., _[Rapaza viridis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapaza\_viridis "Rapaza viridis")_ can only steal from _[Tetraselmis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tetraselmis "Tetraselmis")_ cells).[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Karnkowska-2023-153) The specialists are further divided into two types: _plastidic_, which contain differentiated [plastids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plastid "Plastid") (e.g., _[Mesodinium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesodinium "Mesodinium")_, _[Dinophysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinophysis "Dinophysis")_), and _endosymbiotic_, which contain whole [endosymbionts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosymbiont "Endosymbiont") (e.g., mixotrophic [Rhizaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizaria "Rhizaria") such as [Foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") and [Radiolaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria"), dinoflagellates like _[Noctiluca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noctiluca "Noctiluca")_).[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Mitra-2016-157)

Among exclusively heterotrophic protists, variation of nutritional modes is also observed. The [diplonemids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplonemid "Diplonemid"), which inhabit deep waters where photosynthesis is absent, can flexibly switch between osmotrophy and bacterivory depending on the environmental conditions.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Prokopchuk-2022-159)

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Paramecium_contractile_vacuoles.jpg/250px-Paramecium_contractile_vacuoles.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Paramecium_contractile_vacuoles.jpg)

_[Paramecium aurelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramecium\_aurelia "Paramecium aurelia")_ with [contractile vacuoles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contractile_vacuole "Contractile vacuole")

Many [freshwater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freshwater "Freshwater") protists need to [osmoregulate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmoregulation "Osmoregulation") (i.e., remove excess water volume to adjust the ion concentrations) because non-saline water enters in excess by [osmosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmosis "Osmosis") from the environment[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Patterson-1980-160) and by endocytosis when feeding.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149) Osmoregulation is done through active ion transporters of the cell membrane and through [contractile vacuoles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contractile_vacuole "Contractile vacuole"), specialized [organelles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organelle "Organelle") that periodically excrete fluid high in [potassium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potassium "Potassium") and [sodium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sodium "Sodium") through a cycle of diastole and systole. The cycle stops when the cells are placed in a medium with different salinity, until the cell adapts.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levandowsky-2012-141)

The contractile vacuoles are surrounded by the [spongiome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spongiome "Spongiome"), an array of cytoplasmic vesicles or tubes that slowly collect fluid from the cytoplasm into the vacuole. The vacuoles then contract and discharge the fluid outside of the cell through a pore. The contractile mechanism varies depending on the protist: in ciliates, the spongiome is composed of irregular tubules and [actin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actin "Actin") filaments wind around the pore and over the vacuole surface, together with microtubules; in most flagellates and amoebae, the spongiome is composed of both vesicles and tubules; in dinoflagellates, a flagellar rootlet branches to form a contractile sheath around the vacuole (known as pusule).[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149) The location and amount also varies: unicellular flagellated algae (cryptomonads, euglenids, prasinophytes, golden algae, haptophytes, etc.) typically have a single contractile vacuole in a fixed position; naked amoebae have numerous small vesicles that fuse into one vacuole and then split again after excretion. Marine or parasitic protists (e.g., metamonads), as well as those with rigid cell walls, lack these vacuoles.[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Patterson-1980-160)

The [last eukaryotic common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor") was [aerobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerobic_organism "Aerobic organism"), bearing [mitochondria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondria "Mitochondria") for [oxidative metabolism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxidative_metabolism "Oxidative metabolism"). Many lineages of free-living and parasitic protists have independently evolved and adapted to inhabit [anaerobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental) "Hypoxia (environmental)") or [microaerophilic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microaerophilic "Microaerophilic") habitats, by modifying the early mitochondria into [hydrogenosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogenosome "Hydrogenosome"), organelles that generate [ATP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate "Adenosine triphosphate") anaerobically through [fermentation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fermentation "Fermentation") of [pyruvate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyruvate "Pyruvate"). In a parallel manner, in the microaerophilic [trypanosomatid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trypanosomatid "Trypanosomatid") protists, the fermentative [glycosome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glycosome "Glycosome") evolved from the [peroxisome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peroxisome "Peroxisome").[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levandowsky-2012-141)

[![Image 46: An image of a single cell featuring a large nucleus and an ocelloid, which is composed of a roundish "lens" and a darkly pigmented disc-shaped retinal body.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Bmc_evol_bio_hoppenrath_proterythropsis_ocelloid_fig1a.png/250px-Bmc_evol_bio_hoppenrath_proterythropsis_ocelloid_fig1a.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bmc_evol_bio_hoppenrath_proterythropsis_ocelloid_fig1a.png)

[Light micrograph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_microscopy "Light microscopy") of an [ocelloid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocelloid "Ocelloid")-containing [dinoflagellate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate"). n: [nucleus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus "Cell nucleus"), double arrowhead: ocelloid, scale bar: 10 Î¼m.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hoppenrath-2009-161)

Many flagellates and probably all motile algae exhibit a positive [phototaxis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phototaxis "Phototaxis") (i.e. they swim or glide toward a source of light). For this purpose, they exhibit three kinds of [photoreceptors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photoreceptors,_microbial "Photoreceptors, microbial") or "[eyespots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eyespot_apparatus "Eyespot apparatus")": (1) receptors with light antennae, found in many [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellates "Dinoflagellates") and [cryptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptophytes "Cryptophytes"); (2) receptors with opaque screens; and (3) complex [ocelloids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocelloid "Ocelloid") with intracellular lenses, found in one group of predatory [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate"), the [Warnowiaceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warnowiaceae "Warnowiaceae"). Additionally, some [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliates "Ciliates") orient themselves in relation to the Earth's [gravitational field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitational_field "Gravitational field") while moving ([geotaxis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geotaxis "Geotaxis")), and others swim in relation to the concentration of dissolved [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen "Oxygen") in the water.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levandowsky-2012-141)

Protists have an accentuated tendency to include [endosymbionts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosymbiont "Endosymbiont") in their cells, and these have produced new physiological opportunities. Some associations are more permanent, such as _[Paramecium bursaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramecium\_bursaria "Paramecium bursaria")_ and its endosymbiont _[Chlorella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorella "Chlorella")_; others more transient. Many protists contain captured chloroplasts, chloroplast-mitochondrial complexes, and even eyespots from algae. The [xenosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenosome "Xenosome") are [bacterial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterial "Bacterial") endosymbionts found in ciliates, sometimes with a [methanogenic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methanogenic "Methanogenic") role inside anaerobic ciliates.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levandowsky-2012-141)

Life cycle and reproduction
---------------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Life cycle and reproduction")]

[![Image 47](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Protist-life-cycles-consensus.png/500px-Protist-life-cycles-consensus.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Protist-life-cycles-consensus.png)

Consensus life cycle of free-living protists, including [sexual reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_reproduction "Sexual reproduction") (red arrows), [asexual reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asexual_reproduction "Asexual reproduction") (green arrows), [colonial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_organism "Colonial organism") stages (blue), and formation of [cysts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microbial_cyst "Microbial cyst"). Each protist group has a different sexual cycle (light purple) as well as different means of exiting the colonial stage.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162)

Protists exhibit a large range of [life cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle "Biological life cycle") and [strategies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_strategy "Life strategy") involving multiple stages of different morphologies which have allowed them to thrive in most environments. Nevertheless, most of the knowledge concerning protist life cycles concerns [model organisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_organism "Model organism") and important parasites. Free-living uncultivated protists represent the majority, but knowledge on their life cycles remains fragmentary.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162)

### Asexual reproduction

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Asexual reproduction")]

Protists typically reproduce asexually under favorable environmental conditions,[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Bernstein-2012-163) allowing for rapid exponential population growth with minimal genetic diversification. This [asexual reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asexual_reproduction "Asexual reproduction"), occurs through [mitosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitosis "Mitosis") and has historically been regarded as the primary reproductive mode in protists.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) This process is also known as [vegetative reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetative_reproduction "Vegetative reproduction"), as it is only performed by the 'vegetative stage' or individual.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cecere-2011-164)

Unicellular protists often multiply via [binary fission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_fission "Binary fission"), similarly to bacteria.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) They can also divide through [budding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budding "Budding"), similarly to [yeasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeast "Yeast"), or through multiple fissions, a process known as [schizogony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schizogony "Schizogony").[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Milgroom-2023-165) In multicellular protists, vegetative reproduction can take the form of [fragmentation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fragmentation_(reproduction) "Fragmentation (reproduction)") of body parts, or specialized [propagules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propagules "Propagules") composed of numerous cells (e.g., in [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae")).[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cecere-2011-164)

### Sexual reproduction

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Sexual reproduction")]

While asexual reproduction remains the most common strategy among protists, [sexual reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_reproduction "Sexual reproduction") is also a fundamental characteristic of eukaryotes.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-H%C3%B6randl-2020-166)[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gibson-2021-167) Sexual reproduction involves [meiosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meiosis "Meiosis") (a specialized nuclear division enabling [genetic recombination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_recombination "Genetic recombination")) and [syngamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syngamy "Syngamy") (the fusion of nuclei from two parents).[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) These processes are thought to have been present in the [last eukaryotic common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor"),[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Malik-2007-168) which likely had the ability to reproduce sexually on a facultative (non-obligate) basis.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-169) Even protists that no longer reproduce sexually still retain a core set of meiosis-related genes, reflecting their descent from sexual ancestors.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-170)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-171) For example, although [amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebae "Amoebae") are traditionally considered asexual organisms, most asexual amoebae likely arose recently and independently from sexually reproducing amoeboid ancestors.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lahr-2011-172) Even in the early 20th century, some researchers interpreted phenomena related to chromidia ([chromatin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromatin "Chromatin") granules free in the [cytoplasm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoplasm "Cytoplasm")) in amoebae as sexual reproduction.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Dobell-1909-173)

#### Basic sexual cycles

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Basic sexual cycles")]

Every sexual cycle involves the events of syngamy and meiosis, which increase or decrease the [ploidy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ploidy "Ploidy") (i.e., number of [chromosome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome "Chromosome") sets, represented by the letter _n_), respectively. Syngamy implies the fusion of two haploid (1 _n_) reproductive cells, known as [gametes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gametes "Gametes"), which generates a diploid (2 _n_) cell called [zygote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zygote "Zygote"). The diploid cell then undergoes meiosis to generate haploid cells. Depending on which cells compose the individual or vegetative stage (i.e., the stage that grows by mitosis), there are three distinguishable sexual cycles observed in free-living protists:[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162)

*   In the [haploid cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle#Haplontic_life_cycle "Biological life cycle"), the individual is haploid and [differentiates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_differentiation "Cell differentiation") into haploid gametes through mitosis. The gametes fuse into a zygote which immediately undergoes meiosis to generate new haploid individuals.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) This is the case for some [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae") (namely [Volvocales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvocales "Volvocales")), many [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate"), some [metamonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamonad "Metamonad"), and [apicomplexans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa").[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149): 26 

[![Image 48](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coleps-Konjugation.jpg/150px-Coleps-Konjugation.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Coleps-Konjugation.jpg)

Two ciliates join during conjugation to exchange their haploid nuclei via a cytoplasm bridge.

*   In the [diploid cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle#Diplontic_life_cycle "Biological life cycle"), the individual is diploid and undergoes meiosis to generate haploid gametes, which in turn fuse with others to form a zygote that develops into a new individual.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) This is the case for some metamonads, [heliozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliozoa "Heliozoa"), many green algae, [diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatom "Diatom"), and [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate"), as well as [animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal").[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149): 26  Instead of generating gametes, ciliates divide their diploid [micronucleus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Micronucleus "Micronucleus") into two haploid nuclei, exchange one of them by [conjugation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_conjugation "Sexual conjugation") with another ciliate, and fuse the two nuclei into a new diploid nucleus.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Lynn-2017-71)
*   In the [haplo-diploid cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_life_cycle#Haplodiplontic_life_cycle "Biological life cycle"), there are two [alternating generations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternating_generations "Alternating generations") of individuals. One generation is the diploid 'agamont', which undergoes meiosis to generate haploid cells (spores) that develop into the other generation, the haploid 'gamont'. The gamont then generates gametes by mitosis, which in turn fuse to form the zygote that develops into the agamont.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rizos-2024-162) This is the case for many [foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") and many algae, as well as [land plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte").[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruppert-2004-149): 26  There are three modes of this cycle depending on the relative growth and lifespan of one generation compared to the other: haploid-dominant, diploid-dominant, or equally dominant generations. [Brown algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_algae "Brown algae") exhibit the full range of these modes.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Heesch-2021-174)

Free-living protists tend to reproduce sexually under stressful conditions, such as starvation or heat shock. [Oxidative stress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxidative_stress "Oxidative stress"), which leads to [DNA damage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_repair#DNA_damage "DNA repair"), also appears to be an important factor in the induction of sex in protists.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Bernstein-2012-163)

#### Sexual cycles in pathogenic protists

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Sexual cycles in pathogenic protists")]

Pathogenic protists tend to have extremely complex life cycles that involve multiple forms of the organism, some of which reproduce sexually and others asexually.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-175) The stages that feed and multiply inside the [host](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_(biology) "Host (biology)") are generally known as _[trophozoites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophozoite "Trophozoite")_ (from [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language")_trophos_'nutrition' and _zoia_'animals'), but the names of each stage vary depending on the protist group.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Milgroom-2023-165) For example:

*   In apicomplexans, a haploid _sporozoite_ is released into the host, penetrates a host cell, begins the infection and transforms into a _meront_ that grows and asexually divides into numerous _merozoites_ (a schizogony called _merogony_); each merozoite continues the infection by multiplying. Eventually, the merozoites differentiate (_gamogony_) into female (_macrogametocytes_) and male (_microgametocytes_) that generate gametes, which in turn fuse (_sporogony_) into a diploid zygote that grows into a _sporocyst_. The sporocyst then undergoes meiosis to form sporozoites that transmit the infection.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Vot%C3%BDpka-2017-74)[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gibson-2021-167)
*   In phytomyxeans, the diploid _primary zoospores_ enter the host, encyst, and penetrate cells as a uninucleate _protoplast_ or _plasmodium_. Inside the cells, the protoplast grows into a multinucleate zoosporangium, which then divides into _secondary zoospores_ that infect more cells. These multiply into thick-walled resting spores that begin meiosis and divide into binucleate resting spores; one nucleus is lost, and the spores hatch as primary zoospores.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-176)

Some protist pathogens undergo asexual reproduction in a wide variety of organisms â€“ which act as secondary or intermediate hosts â€“ but can undergo sexual reproduction only in the primary or definitive host (e.g., _[Toxoplasma gondii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toxoplasma\_gondii "Toxoplasma gondii")_ in [felids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felid "Felid") such as [domestic cats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_cat "Domestic cat")).[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-177) Others, such as _[Leishmania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leishmania "Leishmania")_, are capable of performing syngamy in the secondary vector.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-178) In apicomplexans, sexual reproduction is obligatory for parasite transmission.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-da_Silva-2022-179)

Despite undergoing sexual reproduction, it is unclear how frequently there is genetic exchange between different strains of pathogenic protists, as most populations may be clonal lines that rarely exchange genes with other members of their species.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-180)

Protists are indispensable to modern [ecosystems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem "Ecosystem") worldwide. They also have been the only eukaryotic component of all ecosystems for much of [Earth's history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_history "Earth's history"), which allowed them to evolve a vast functional diversity that explains their critical ecological significance. They are essential as [primary producers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_producer "Primary producer"), as intermediates in multiple [trophic levels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_level "Trophic level"), as key regulating [parasites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasite "Parasite") or [parasitoids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitoid "Parasitoid"), and as partners in diverse [symbioses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbioses "Symbioses").[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Burki-2021-40)

Protists are abundant and diverse in nearly all habitats. They contribute 4 gigatons (Gt) to Earth's biomassâ€”double that of animals (2 Gt), but less than 1% of the total. Combined, protists, animals, archaea (7 Gt), and fungi (12 Gt) make up less than 10% of global biomass, with plants (450 Gt) and bacteria (70 Gt) dominating.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Bar-On-2018-181) Protist diversity, as detected through [environmental DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA") surveys, is vast in every sampled environment, but it is mostly undescribed.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Epstein-2007-182) The richest protist communities appear in [soils](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil "Soil"), followed by [oceanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean "Ocean") and lastly [freshwater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freshwater "Freshwater") habitats, mostly as part of the [plankton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plankton "Plankton").[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183) Freshwater protist communities are characterized by a higher "beta diversity" (i.e. highly heterogeneous between samples) than soil and marine plankton. The high diversity can be a result of the hydrological dynamic of recruiting organisms from different habitats through extreme [floods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flood "Flood").[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Metz-2022-184)[Soil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil "Soil")-dwelling protist communities are ecologically the richest, possibly be due to the complex and highly dynamic distribution of water in the [sediment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sediment "Sediment"), which creates extremely heterogenous environmental conditions. The constantly changing environment promotes the activity of only one part of the community at a time, while the rest remains inactive; this phenomenon promotes high microbial diversity in [prokaryotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryotes "Prokaryotes") as well as protists.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183)

Microscopic phototrophic protists (or [microalgae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microalgae "Microalgae")) are the main contributors to the [biomass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass "Biomass") and [primary production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_production "Primary production") in nearly all aquatic environments, where they are collectively known as [phytoplankton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytoplankton "Phytoplankton") (together with [cyanobacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanobacteria "Cyanobacteria")). In marine phytoplankton, the smallest fractions, the picoplankton (<2 Î¼m) and nanoplankton (2â€“20 Î¼m), are dominated by several different algae ([prymnesiophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prymnesiophyte "Prymnesiophyte"), [pelagophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pelagophyte "Pelagophyte"), [prasinophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prasinophyte "Prasinophyte")); fractions larger than 5 Î¼m are instead dominated by [diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatom "Diatom") and [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate").[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Epstein-2007-182) In freshwater phytoplankton, [golden algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_algae "Golden algae"), [cryptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptophyte "Cryptophyte") and dinoflagellates are the most abundant groups.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183) Altogether, they are responsible for almost half of the global primary production.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Thor%C3%A9-2023-185) They are the main providers of much of the energy and organic matter used by [bacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria "Bacteria"), [archaea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaea "Archaea"), and higher trophic levels ([zooplankton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zooplankton "Zooplankton") and [fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish "Fish")), including essential nutrients such as [fatty acids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatty_acid "Fatty acid").[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Caron-2009-186) Their abundance in the oceans depends mostly on the availability of inorganic nutrients, rather than temperature or sunlight; they are most abundant in coastal waters that receive nutrient-rich run-off from land, and areas where nutrient-rich deep ocean water reaches the surface, namely the upwelling zones in the [Arctic Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_Ocean "Arctic Ocean") and along [continental margins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_margin "Continental margin").[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Thor%C3%A9-2023-185) In freshwater habitats, most phototrophic protists are [mixotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixotroph "Mixotroph"), meaning they also behave as consumers, while strict consumers (heterotrophs) are less abundant.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183)

[Macroalgae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macroalgae "Macroalgae") (namely [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae"), [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae") and [brown algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_algae "Brown algae")), unlike phytoplankton, generally require a fixation point, which limits their marine distribution to coastal waters, and particularly to rocky substrates. They support numerous herbivorous animals, especially [benthic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benthic "Benthic") ones, as both food and refuge from predators. Some communities of [seaweeds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seaweed "Seaweed") exist adrift on the ocean surface, serving as a refuge and means of dispersal for associated organisms.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-187)[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-188)

Phototrophic protists are as abundant in soils as their aquatic counterparts. Given the importance of aquatic algae, soil algae may provide a larger contribution to the global [carbon cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_cycle "Carbon cycle") than previously thought, but the magnitude of their carbon fixation has yet to be quantified.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183) Most soil algae are [stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stramenopiles "Stramenopiles") ([diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatom "Diatom"), [xanthophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xanthophyte "Xanthophyte") and [eustigmatophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eustigmatophyte "Eustigmatophyte")) and [archaeplastids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeplastid "Archaeplastid") ([green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae")). There is also presence of [environmental DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA") from [dinoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinoflagellate "Dinoflagellate") and [haptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptophyte "Haptophyte") in soil, but no living forms have been seen.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189)

[Phagotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagotroph "Phagotroph") protists are the most diverse functional group in all ecosystems, primarily represented by [cercozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cercozoa "Cercozoa") (dominant in freshwater and soils), [radiolarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria") (dominant in oceans), non-photosynthetic [stramenopiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stramenopile "Stramenopile") (with higher abundance in soils than in oceans), and [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate").[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183)

Contrary to the common division between phytoplankton and zooplankton, much of the marine plankton is composed of [mixotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixotrophic "Mixotrophic") protists, which pose a largely underestimated importance and abundance (around 12% of all marine [environmental DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_DNA "Environmental DNA") sequences). Mixotrophs have varied presence due to [seasonal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Season "Season") abundance[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Leles-2017-190) and depending on their specific type of mixotrophy. Constitutive mixotrophs are present in almost the entire range of oceanic conditions, from eutrophic shallow habitats to oligotrophic subtropical waters but mostly dominating the [photic zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photic_zone "Photic zone"), and they account for most of the predation of bacteria. They are also responsible for [harmful algal blooms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmful_algal_bloom "Harmful algal bloom"). Plastidic and generalist non-constitutive mixotrophs have similar biogeographies and low abundance, mostly found in eutrophic coastal waters, with generalist [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate") dominating up to half of ciliate communities in the photic zone. Lastly, endosymbiotic mixotrophs are by far the most widespread and abundant non-constitutive type, representing over 90% of all mixotroph sequences (mostly [radiolarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria")).[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Faure-2019-158)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Mitra-2016-157)

[![Image 49](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Protist_soil_food_web.svg/330px-Protist_soil_food_web.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Protist_soil_food_web.svg)

Diagram of the soil food web, taking into account the diverse roles of protists as not just bacterivores, but also mycophages and omnivores.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2016-151) Arrows show the flow of nutrients.

In the [trophic webs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trophic_web "Trophic web") of soils, protists are the main consumers of both [bacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria "Bacteria") and [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi"), the two main pathways of nutrient flow towards higher trophic levels.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Harder-2016-191) Amoeboflagellates like the [glissomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glissomonad "Glissomonad") and [cercomonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cercomonad "Cercomonad") are among the most abundant soil protists: they possess both flagella and pseudopodia, a morphological variability well suited for foraging between soil particles. Testate amoebae are also acclimated to the soil environment, as their shells protect against [desiccation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desiccation "Desiccation").[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189) As bacterial grazers, they have a significant role in the foodweb: they excrete [nitrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen "Nitrogen") in the form of [NH 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ammonia "Ammonia"), making it available to plants and other microbes.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Harder-2016-191) Traditionally, protists were considered primarily bacterivorous due to biases in cultivation techniques, but many (e.g., [vampyrellids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampyrellid "Vampyrellid"), cercomonads, gymnamoebae, [testate amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testate_amoebae "Testate amoebae"), small flagellates) are omnivores that feed on a wide range of soil eukaryotes, including fungi and even some animals such as [nematodes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nematode "Nematode"). Bacterivorous and mycophagous protists amount to similar biomasses.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2016-151)

[Necrophagy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Necrophagy "Necrophagy") (the degradation of dead biomass) among microbes is mainly attributed to bacteria and fungi, but protists have a still poorly recognized role as [decomposers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decomposer "Decomposer") with specialized [lytic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lysis "Lysis")[enzymes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enzyme "Enzyme").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Moye-2024-192) In soils, [fungus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus")-like protists and [slime molds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slime_mold "Slime mold") (e.g., [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycete "Oomycete"), [myxomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxomycete "Myxomycete"), [acrasids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acrasid "Acrasid")) are present abundantly as [osmotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmotroph "Osmotroph") and [saprotrophs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saprotroph "Saprotroph").[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189) In marine and estuarine environments, the well-studied [thraustochytrids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thraustochytrid "Thraustochytrid") (part of [labyrinthulomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labyrinthulomycetes "Labyrinthulomycetes")) are relevant saprotrophs that decompose various substrates, including dead plant and animal tissue. Various ciliates and testate amoebae scavenge on dead animals. Some [nucleariid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleariid "Nucleariid") amoebae specifically consume the contents of dead or damaged cells, but not healthy cells. However, all these examples are only facultative necrophages that also feed on live prey. In contrast, the algivorous cercozoan family [Viridiraptoridae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viridiraptoridae "Viridiraptoridae"), present in shallow bog waters, are broad-range but sophisticated necrophages that feed on a variety of exclusively dead algae, potentially fulfilling an important role in cleaning up the environment and releasing nutrients for live microbes.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Moye-2024-192)

### Parasites and pathogens

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Parasites and pathogens")]

[Parasitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitic "Parasitic") protists occupy around 15â€“20% of all environmental DNA in marine and soil systems, but only around 5% in freshwater systems, where [chytrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chytrid "Chytrid") fungi likely fill that [ecological niche](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_niche "Ecological niche"). In oceanic systems, [parasitoids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parasitoid "Parasitoid") (i.e. those which kill their hosts, e.g. [Syndiniales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syndiniales "Syndiniales")) are more abundant. In freshwater ecosystems, parasitoids are mainly [Perkinsea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perkinsea "Perkinsea") and [Syndiniales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syndiniales "Syndiniales") (Alveolata), while true parasites (i.e. those which do not kill their hosts) in freshwater are mostly [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycetes "Oomycetes"), [Apicomplexa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa") and [Ichthyosporea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ichthyosporea "Ichthyosporea").[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183) In soil ecosystems, true parasites are primarily animal-hosted [apicomplexans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa") and plant-hosted [oomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycetes "Oomycetes") and [plasmodiophorids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmodiophorid "Plasmodiophorid").[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189) In [Neotropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neotropical "Neotropical") forest soils, apicomplexans dominate eukaryotic diversity and have an important role as parasites of small invertebrates, while oomycetes are very scarce in contrast.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-193)

Some protists are significant parasites of animals (e.g.; five species of the parasitic genus _[Plasmodium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasmodium "Plasmodium")_ cause [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria") in humans and many others cause similar diseases in other vertebrates), land plants[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-194)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-195) (the [oomycete](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oomycete "Oomycete")_[Phytophthora infestans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytophthora\_infestans "Phytophthora infestans")_ causes [late blight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_blight "Late blight") in potatoes)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-196) or even of other protists.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-197)[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-198) Around 100 protist species can infect humans.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189)

### Biogeochemical cycles

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Biogeochemical cycles")]

[Marine protists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marine_protists "Marine protists") have a fundamental impact on [biogeochemical cycles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeochemical_cycle "Biogeochemical cycle"), particularly the [carbon cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_cycle "Carbon cycle").[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Keeling-2017-199) As phytoplankton, they [fix as much carbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_fixation "Carbon fixation") as all [terrestrial plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrestrial_plant "Terrestrial plant") combined.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Singer-2021-183) Soil protists, particularly [testate amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testate_amoebae "Testate amoebae"), contribute to the [silica cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silica_cycle "Silica cycle") as much as forest trees through the biomineralization of their shells.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Geisen-2018-189)

History of classification
-------------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: History of classification")]

### Early classification

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Early classification")]

[![Image 50](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Egg_tree_of_animals_Goldfuss_1820.jpg/250px-Egg_tree_of_animals_Goldfuss_1820.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Egg_tree_of_animals_Goldfuss_1820.jpg)

[Goldfuss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georg_August_Goldfuss "Georg August Goldfuss")' system of life, introducing the Protozoa within animals.

From the start of the 18th century, the popular term "infusion animals" (later [infusoria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infusoria "Infusoria")) was used for protists, [bacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria "Bacteria") and small [invertebrates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invertebrate "Invertebrate"). In the mid-18th century, while Swedish biologist [Carl Linnaeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus "Carl Linnaeus") largely ignored the protists,[[f]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-201) his Danish contemporary [Otto Friedrich MÃ¼ller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller "Otto Friedrich MÃ¼ller") was the first to introduce protists to the [binomial nomenclature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature "Binomial nomenclature") system.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Leadbeater-2000-200)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ratcliff-2009-202)

In 1820, German naturalist [Georg August Goldfuss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georg_August_Goldfuss "Georg August Goldfuss") coined the term "[Protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa")" (meaning 'early animals') as a class within Kingdom Animalia[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Goldfu%C3%9F-1818-203) that consisted of four groups: [Infusoria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infusoria "Infusoria") ([ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliates "Ciliates")), Lithozoa ([corals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coral "Coral")), Phytozoa, and Medusinae ([jellyfish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jellyfish "Jellyfish")). Later, in 1845, [Carl Theodor von Siebold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Theodor_von_Siebold "Carl Theodor von Siebold") used the term "[Protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa")" as a phylum of exclusively unicellular animals consisting of two classes: Infusoria (ciliates) and [Rhizopoda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhizopoda "Rhizopoda") ([amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebae "Amoebae"), [foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera")).[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Siebold-1848-204) Other scientists did not consider all protozoans part of the animal kingdom, and by the middle of the century most biologists grouped microorganisms into Protozoa, Protophyta (primitive plants), Phytozoa (animal-like plants), and [Bacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacteria "Bacteria") (mostly considered plants). In 1860, palaeontolgist [Richard Owen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Owen "Richard Owen") was the first to define Protozoa as its own kingdom of eukaryotes, although he also included [sponges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sponges "Sponges") within his group.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)

[![Image 51](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/John_Hogg_--_Primigenum_or_Protoctista.jpg/500px-John_Hogg_--_Primigenum_or_Protoctista.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:John_Hogg_--_Primigenum_or_Protoctista.jpg)

[John Hogg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Hogg_(biologist) "John Hogg (biologist)")'s illustration of the Four Kingdoms of Nature, showing _"Regnum Primigenum"_ (Protoctista) as a greenish haze at the base of the Animals and Plants, 1860

In 1860, British naturalist [John Hogg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Hogg_(biologist) "John Hogg (biologist)") proposed "Protoctista" as the name for a fourth kingdom, (the other kingdoms being plant, animal and mineral) which he described as containing "all the lower creatures, or the primary organic beings", which included Protophyta, Protozoa and [sponges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sponge "Sponge").[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hogg-1860-205)[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)

[![Image 52](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Haeckel_arbol_bn.png/250px-Haeckel_arbol_bn.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Haeckel_arbol_bn.png)

[Haeckel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Haeckel "Ernst Haeckel")'s 1866 tree of life, with the third kingdom Protista.

In 1866, the 'father of protistology', German scientist [Ernst Haeckel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernst_Haeckel "Ernst Haeckel"), addressed the problem of classifying all these organisms as a mixture of animal and vegetable characters, and proposed _Protistenreich_[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Haeckel-1878-206) (Kingdom Protista) as the [third kingdom of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#Three_kingdoms_of_life "Kingdom (biology)"), comprising primitive forms that were "neither animals nor plants". He grouped both bacteria[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Taylor-2003-207) and eukaryotes, both unicellular and multicellular organisms, as Protista. He retained the [Infusoria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infusoria "Infusoria") in the animal kingdom, until German zoologist [Otto BÃ¼tschli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_B%C3%BCtschli "Otto BÃ¼tschli") demonstrated that they were unicellular.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Haeckel-1866-208)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Rothschild-1989-209) At first, he included [sponges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sponges "Sponges") and fungi, but in later publications he explicitly restricted Protista to predominantly unicellular organisms or colonies incapable of forming [tissues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tissue_(biology) "Tissue (biology)"). He clearly separated Protista from [true animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metazoa "Metazoa") on the basis that the defining character of protists was the absence of [sexual reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_reproduction "Sexual reproduction"), while the defining character of animals was the [blastula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blastula "Blastula") stage of animal development. He also returned the terms _Protozoa_ and _Protophyta_ as subkingdoms of Protista.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)

### End of the animal-plant dichotomy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: End of the animal-plant dichotomy")]

BÃ¼tschli considered the kingdom to be too [polyphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyphyletic "Polyphyletic") and rejected the inclusion of bacteria. He fragmented the kingdom into _protozoa_ (only nucleated, unicellular animal-like organisms), while bacteria and the _protophyta_ were a separate grouping. This strengthened the old dichotomy of _protozoa_/_protophyta_ from German scientist [Carl Theodor von Siebold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Theodor_von_Siebold "Carl Theodor von Siebold"), and the German naturalists asserted this view over the worldwide scientific community by the turn of the century. However, British biologist [C. Clifford Dobell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C._Clifford_Dobell "C. Clifford Dobell") in 1911 brought attention to the fact that protists functioned very differently compared to the animal and vegetable cellular organization, and gave importance to Protista as a group with a different organization that he called "acellularity", shifting away from the dogma of German cell theory. He coined the term [protistology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protistology "Protistology") and solidified it as a branch of study independent from [zoology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoology "Zoology") and [botany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Botany "Botany").[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)

In 1938, American biologist [Herbert Copeland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_Copeland_(biologist) "Herbert Copeland (biologist)") resurrected Hogg's label, arguing that Haeckel's term _Protista_ included anucleated microbes such as bacteria, which the term _Protoctista_ (meaning "first established beings") did not. Under his [four-kingdom classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#Four_kingdoms "Kingdom (biology)") ([Monera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monera "Monera"), _Protoctista_, [Plantae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantae "Plantae"), [Animalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animalia "Animalia")), the protists and bacteria were finally split apart, recognizing the difference between anucleate ([prokaryotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryotic "Prokaryotic")) and nucleate ([eukaryotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic "Eukaryotic")) organisms. To firmly separate protists from plants, he followed Haeckel's blastular definition of true animals, and proposed defining [true plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyta "Embryophyta") as those with [chlorophyll _a_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyll_a "Chlorophyll a") and [_b_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyll_b "Chlorophyll b"), [carotene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carotene "Carotene"), [xanthophyll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xanthophyll "Xanthophyll") and production of [starch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starch "Starch"). He also was the first to recognize that the unicellular/multicellular dichotomy was invalid. Still, he kept fungi within Protoctista, together with [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae"), [brown algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_algae "Brown algae") and [protozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa").[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Copeland-1938-210) This classification was the basis for Whittaker's later definition of Fungi, [Animalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animalia "Animalia"), [Plantae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantae "Plantae") and Protista as the four kingdoms of life.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Whittaker-1959-211)

In the popular [five-kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#Five_kingdoms "Kingdom (biology)") scheme published by American plant ecologist [Robert Whittaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Whittaker_(ecologist) "Robert Whittaker (ecologist)") in 1969, Protista was defined as eukaryotic "organisms which are [unicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicellular_organism "Unicellular organism") or unicellular-colonial and which form no [tissues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tissue_(biology) "Tissue (biology)")". Just as the prokaryotic/eukaryotic division was becoming mainstream, Whittaker, after a decade from Copeland's system,[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Whittaker-1959-211) recognized the fundamental division of life between the prokaryotic Monera and the eukaryotic kingdoms: Animalia (ingestion), Plantae (photosynthesis), Fungi (absorption) and the remaining Protista.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Whittaker-1969-212)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Hagen-2012-213)[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Scamardella-1999-30)

In the five-kingdom system of American evolutionary biologist [Lynn Margulis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynn_Margulis "Lynn Margulis"), the term "protist" was reserved for [microscopic organisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microscopic_organisms "Microscopic organisms"), while the more inclusive kingdom Protoctista (or **protoctists**) included certain large [multicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellular_organism "Multicellular organism") eukaryotes, such as [kelp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelp "Kelp"), [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae"), and [slime molds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slime_mold "Slime mold").[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-214) Some use the term _protist_ interchangeably with Margulis' _protoctist_, to encompass both single-celled and multicellular eukaryotes, including those that form specialized tissues but do not fit into any of the other traditional kingdoms.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Archibald-2017-215)

### Advances in electron microscopy and molecular phylogenetics

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Advances in electron microscopy and molecular phylogenetics")]

[![Image 53](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Eukaryotic_tree_of_life_%28Burki_et_al_2020%29.jpg/500px-Eukaryotic_tree_of_life_%28Burki_et_al_2020%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Eukaryotic_tree_of_life_(Burki_et_al_2020).jpg)

Phylogenomic tree of eukaryotes, as regarded in 2020. [Supergroups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supergroup_(biology) "Supergroup (biology)") are in color.

The five-kingdom model remained the accepted classification until the development of [molecular phylogenetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_phylogenetic "Molecular phylogenetic") in the late 20th century, when it became apparent that protists are a [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyly "Paraphyly") group from which animals, fungi and land plants evolved, and the [three-domain system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-domain_system "Three-domain system") (Bacteria, [Archaea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaea "Archaea"), [Eukarya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukarya "Eukarya")) became prevalent.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Stechmann-2003-216) Today, protists are not treated as a formal [taxon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxon "Taxon"), but the term is commonly used for convenience in two ways:[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-O'Malley-2012-14)

*   [Phylogenetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylogenetic "Phylogenetic") definition: protists are a [paraphyletic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paraphyly "Paraphyly") group.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Schlegel-2007-217) A protist is any [eukaryote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote "Eukaryote") that is not an animal, land plant or fungus,[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-microbeworld-218) thus excluding many unicellular groups like the fungal [Microsporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsporidia "Microsporidia"), [Chytridiomycetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chytridiomycetes "Chytridiomycetes") and [yeasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yeast "Yeast"), and the non-unicellular [Myxozoan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxozoa "Myxozoa") animals included in Protista in the past.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-219)
*   Functional definition: protists are essentially those eukaryotes that are never [multicellular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellular "Multicellular"),[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-O'Malley-2012-14) that either exist as independent cells, or if they occur in [colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_organism "Colonial organism"), do not show differentiation into tissues.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2005-220) While in popular usage, this definition excludes the variety of non-colonial multicellularity types that protists exhibit, such as aggregative (e.g., [choanoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choanoflagellates "Choanoflagellates")) or complex multicellularity (e.g., [brown algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_algae "Brown algae")).[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-O'Malley-2022-221)

There is, however, one classification of protists based on traditional ranks that lasted until the 21st century.
