The British protozoologist [Thomas Cavalier-Smith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Cavalier-Smith "Thomas Cavalier-Smith"), since 1998, developed a [six-kingdom model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#Six_kingdoms_(1998) "Kingdom (biology)"):[[g]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-223) Bacteria, [Animalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animalia "Animalia"), [Plantae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantae "Plantae"), Fungi, _[Protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa")_ and _[Chromista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromista "Chromista")_.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-1998-10)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruggiero-2015-222) In his context, paraphyletic groups take preference over clades:[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-1998-10) both protist kingdoms _Protozoa_ and _Chromista_ contain paraphyletic [phyla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phylum "Phylum") such as [Apusozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apusozoa "Apusozoa"), [Eolouka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eolouka "Eolouka") or [Opisthosporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthosporidia "Opisthosporidia"). Additionally, [red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae") and [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae") are considered true plants, while the [fungal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungal "Fungal") groups [Microsporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsporidia "Microsporidia"), [Rozellida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rozellida "Rozellida") and [Aphelida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphelida "Aphelida") are considered protozoans under the phylum [Opisthosporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthosporidia "Opisthosporidia"). This scheme endured until 2021, the year of his last publication.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2022-9)

Before the existence of [land plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte"), [animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal") and [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus"), all [eukaryotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote "Eukaryote") were protists. As a result, the early fossil record of protists is equivalent to the early record of eukaryotic life.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-da_Silva-2022-179) The protist fossil record is mainly represented by protists with fossilizable coverings, such as foraminifera, radiolaria, testate amoebae and diatoms, as well as multicellular algae.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)

### Paleo- and Mesoproterozoic

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protist&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Paleo- and Mesoproterozoic")]

Modern or _[crown-group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown-group "Crown-group")_ eukaryotes originated from the [last eukaryotic common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_eukaryotic_common_ancestor "Last eukaryotic common ancestor") (LECA) and emerged between 1600 and 2400 million years ago (Ma), during the [Paleoproterozoic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleoproterozoic "Paleoproterozoic") and [Mesoproterozoic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesoproterozoic "Mesoproterozoic") eras.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Strassert-2021-1) However, the [fossil record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_record "Fossil record") through this time is scarce and dominated by _[stem-group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stem-group "Stem-group")_ eukaryotes, extinct lineages preceding LECA. These lineages displayed early eukaryotic traits like flexible [cell membranes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_membrane "Cell membrane") and complex [cell wall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_wall "Cell wall") ornamentations, which require a flexible [endomembrane system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endomembrane_system "Endomembrane system"), but they lacked crown-group eukaryotes' advanced sterols (e.g., [cholesterol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cholesterol "Cholesterol")), and instead produced simpler [protosterols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protosterol_biota "Protosterol biota") that require less [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen "Oxygen") during [biosynthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosynthesis "Biosynthesis").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) Examples of these are: _[Trachyhystrichosphaera](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Trachyhystrichosphaera&action=edit&redlink=1 "Trachyhystrichosphaera (page does not exist)")_ and _[Leiosphaeridia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leiosphaeridia "Leiosphaeridia")_ dated at 1100 Ma,[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-226)_[Satka](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Satka\_(genus)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Satka (genus) (page does not exist)")_ dated at 1300 Ma,[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-227)_[Tappania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tappania "Tappania")_ and _[Shuiyousphaeridium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuiyousphaeridium "Shuiyousphaeridium")_ dated at 1600 Ma,[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-228)_[Grypania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grypania "Grypania")_ dated at 1800â€“1900 Ma, and _Valeria_ which ranges from 1650 to 700 Ma.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Xiao-2013-229)

Crown-group eukaryotes achieved significant [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology) "Morphology (biology)") and [ecological diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecological_diversity "Ecological diversity") before 1000 Ma, with multicellular algae capable of sexual reproduction and unicellular protists exhibiting modern [phagocytosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phagocytosis "Phagocytosis") and [locomotion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist_locomotion "Protist locomotion"). Their advanced but metabolically expensive sterols likely provided numerous [evolutionary advantages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptation "Adaptation") due to the increased membrane flexibility, including resilience to [osmotic shock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osmotic_shock "Osmotic shock") during desiccation and rehydration cycles, extreme temperatures, [UV light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UV_light "UV light") exposure, and protection against [changing oxygen levels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Oxidation_Event "Great Oxidation Event"). These adaptations allowed crown-group eukaryotes to colonize diverse and harsh environments (e.g., [mudflats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mudflat "Mudflat"), rivers, agitated shorelines and land). In contrast, stem-group eukaryotes occupied the low-oxygen marine waters as [anaerobes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaerobe "Anaerobe").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) The oldest definitive crown-group eukaryotic fossils include _[Rafatazmia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafatazmia "Rafatazmia")_ and _[Ramathallus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramathallus "Ramathallus")_, both putative red algae, dated at 1600 Ma.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Strassert-2021-1)

As oxygen levels rose during the [Tonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tonian "Tonian") period, crown-group eukaryotes outcompeted stem-group eukaryotes, expanding into oxygen-rich marine environments that supported an [aerobic metabolism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerobic_metabolism "Aerobic metabolism") enabled by their [mitochondria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondria "Mitochondria"). Stem-group eukaryotes may have gone extinct due to competition and the extreme climatic changes of the [Cryogenian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryogenian "Cryogenian")[glaciations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glaciations "Glaciations") and subsequent [global warming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_warming "Global warming"), cementing the dominance of crown-group eukaryotes.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) Crown-group eukaryotes began to appear abundantly in this era, fueled by the proliferation of [red algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae"). The oldest fossils firmly assigned to existing protist groups include three multicellular algae: the [rhodophyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhodophyte "Rhodophyte")_[Bangiomorpha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangiomorpha "Bangiomorpha")_ (1047 Ma),[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Gibson-2017-230) the [chlorophyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorophyte "Chlorophyte")_[Proterocladus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proterocladus "Proterocladus")_ (1000 Ma),[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) and the [xanthophyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xanthophyceae "Xanthophyceae")_[Paleovaucheria](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paleovaucheria&action=edit&redlink=1 "Paleovaucheria (page does not exist)")_ (1000 Ma).[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Butterfield-2004-231)[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-232) Also included are the oldest fossils of [Opisthokonta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthokonta "Opisthokonta"): _[Ourasphaira giraldae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ourasphaira\_giraldae "Ourasphaira giraldae")_ (1010â€“890 Ma), interpreted as the earliest [fungus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus"),[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) and _[Bicellum brasieri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicellum\_brasieri "Bicellum brasieri")_ (1000 Ma), the earliest [holozoan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holozoan "Holozoan"), showing traits associated with complex [multicellularity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicellularity "Multicellularity").[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Strother-2021-233)

Abundant fossils of [heterotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotrophic "Heterotrophic") protists appear significantly later, parallel to the emergence of [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brocks-2023-225) Vase-shaped microfossils (VSMs), widespread rocks dated at 780â€“720 Ma (Tonian to Cryogenian), have been described as a variety of organisms across the decades (e.g., algae, [chitinozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chitinozoa "Chitinozoa"), [tintinnids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tintinnid "Tintinnid")), but current scientific consensus relates most VSMs to marine [testate amoebae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testate_amoebae "Testate amoebae").[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Chai-2021-234) As such, VSMs comprise the oldest known fossils of both filose ([Cercozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cercozoa "Cercozoa")) and lobose ([Amoebozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amoebozoa "Amoebozoa")) testate amoebae.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Porter-2003-235)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Parfrey-2011-236)

After the [Gaskiers glaciation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaskiers_glaciation "Gaskiers glaciation") of the [Late Ediacaran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ediacaran "Ediacaran") (~579 Ma), fossils of heterotrophic protists undergo diversification. Some fossils similar to VSMs are interpreted as the oldest fossils of [Foraminifera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foraminifera "Foraminifera") dated at 548 Ma (e.g., _[Protolagena](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Protolagena&action=edit&redlink=1 "Protolagena (page does not exist)")_),[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Chai-2021-234) but their foraminiferal affinity is doubtful. Other microfossils that are possibly foraminifera include some poorly preserved tubular shells from 716â€“635 Ma rocks.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Xiao-2021-237)

[Radiolarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiolaria "Radiolaria") shells appear abundantly in the fossil record since the [Cambrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambrian "Cambrian"), with the first definitive radiolarian fossils found at the very start of this period (~540 Ma) together with the first [small shelly fauna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_shelly_fauna "Small shelly fauna").[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Braun-2007-238) Radiolarian records from older [Precambrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precambrian "Precambrian") rocks have been disregarded due to the lack of reliable fossils.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Chang-2018-239)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Zhang-2019-240)[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Maletz-2017-241) Around this time, between 540 and 510 Ma, the oldest Foraminifera shells appear, first multi-chambered and later tubular.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Pawlowski-2003-242)[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Xiao-2021-237)

Following the [Cambrian explosion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambrian_explosion "Cambrian explosion") and rapid diversification of animals, the Precambrian microbe-dominated ecosystems were replaced by primarily [benthic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benthic "Benthic") and nekto-benthic communities, with most marine organisms (animals, foraminifers, radiolarians) limited to the depths of shallow water environments.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Servais-2016-243) Mirroring the animal [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_radiation "Evolutionary radiation"), there was a radiation of phytoplanktonic protists (i.e., acritarchs)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Vecoli-2004-244) around 520â€“510 Ma, followed by a decrease in diversity around 500 Ma.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-245) Later, the surviving acritarchs expanded in diversity and morphological innovation[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Vecoli-2004-244) due to a decrease in predation from benthic animals (particularly [trilobites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trilobite "Trilobite") and [brachiopods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brachiopod "Brachiopod")), which suffered extinction due to various proposed environmental factors such as [anoxia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anoxic_event "Anoxic event").[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Zhang-2023-246) Both phytoplankton and zooplankton (e.g., radiolarians) flourished, as signaled by an increase of organic carbon buried in the sediment known as the [SPICE event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steptoean_positive_carbon_isotope_excursion "Steptoean positive carbon isotope excursion") (~497 Ma).[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Servais-2016-243)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Zhang-2023-246) This abundant [biomass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass "Biomass") supported a second animal radiation known as the [Great Ordovician Biodiversification Event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Ordovician_Biodiversification_Event "Great Ordovician Biodiversification Event") (GOBE), where many animals switched to a planktonic lifestyle and pelagic predators first appeared (e.g., [cephalopods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cephalopod "Cephalopod"), swimming [arthropods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthropod "Arthropod")). This event is also known as the 'Ordovician Plankton Revolution' due to the significant diversification of planktonic protists, and it spanned from the late Cambrian well into the [Ordovician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordovician "Ordovician").[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Servais-2016-243)

The Ordovician also includes the oldest [euglenid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euglenid "Euglenid") fossil, known as _[Moyeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moyeria "Moyeria")_, which is found in rocks spanning from the middle Ordovician (~471 Ma) to the [Silurian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silurian "Silurian").[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Strother-2020-247) There are putative records of calcareous foraminifera from the Early Ordovician to the Silurian, but these are not widely accepted; the oldest trusted and well-known calcaerous foraminifera appear in the Middle [Devonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devonian "Devonian"), the next geological period.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-248)

In Early Devonian terrestrial ecosystems the first fossils of freshwater arcellinid testate amoebae are found (e.g., _Palaeoleptochlamys_, _Cangweulla_),[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-249) as well as various types of freshwater [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae"), including [charophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charophyte "Charophyte"), [volvocaceans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvocaceae "Volvocaceae") and [desmids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desmid "Desmid"),[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-250) and some putative algal fossils that might represent [glaucophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glaucophyte "Glaucophyte").[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-251) During the Devonian some benthic foraminifera acquired the ability of calcifying, and particularly the giant [fusulinids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fusulinida "Fusulinida") became the dominant fossilizable protists. This time interval is also considered the molecular origin of [haptophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haptophyte "Haptophyte") (~310 Ma) and [silicoflagellates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicoflagellate "Silicoflagellate") (397â€“382 Ma), which did not leave fossil traces until later in the [Mesozoic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesozoic "Mesozoic"). After the [Late Devonian extinction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Devonian_extinction "Late Devonian extinction") (372 Ma), [nassellarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nassellaria "Nassellaria")-like radiolarians appeared for the first time, with a unique [body plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_plan "Body plan") among marine protists.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)

During the [Carboniferous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carboniferous "Carboniferous") period, no new fossilizable protists originated despite the major environmental changes. However, starting in the Late Carboniferous, radiolarian diversity and productivity increased, causing a large amount of biosiliceous sediment ([chert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chert "Chert")) to be accumulated worldwide; this is known as the Radiolarian Optimum Event, which lasted primarily from the Middle [Permian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permian "Permian") until the Early [Cretaceous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cretaceous "Cretaceous").[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wever-2007-252)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-253)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-254) Around the [Capitanian mass extinction event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitanian_mass_extinction_event "Capitanian mass extinction event") (262â€“259 Ma) of the Permian period, [coccolithophores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coccolithophore "Coccolithophore") genetically diverged from the rest of haptophytes, possibly as a response to a reduction in atmospheric oxygen, and there was a faunal turnover from larger to smaller fusulinids.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)[Spumellarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spumellaria "Spumellaria") radiolarians appear in the latest Permian.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wever-2007-252)

The [Permian-Triassic extinction event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permian-Triassic_extinction_event "Permian-Triassic extinction event") (~251.9 Ma) caused the extinction of many radiolarians, which manifests as a gap in the chert record.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wever-2007-252) The extinction is hypothesized as resulting in the molecular origin of [diatoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diatoms "Diatoms") and modern coccolithophores.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224) The Middle to Late [Triassic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triassic "Triassic") period saw the acceleration of radiolarian diversity[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wever-2007-252) and the appearance of several groups of calcaerous nannofossils. First, various nannofossils, some of which belonged to [dinocysts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinocysts "Dinocysts"), appeared early at around 235 Ma. Later originated the oldest identifiable coccolithophore, _[Crucirhabdus minutus](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Crucirhabdus\_minutus&action=edit&redlink=1 "Crucirhabdus minutus (page does not exist)")_ (205â€“201 Ma), as well as the oldest fossils of [Phaeodaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phaeodaria "Phaeodaria").[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224) There's a variety of protozoa, including soft-bodied [ciliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciliate "Ciliate"), and filamentous algae found in [amber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amber "Amber") from the Late Triassic (220â€“230 Ma).[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Poinar-1993-255)

Around the Earlyâ€“Middle [Jurassic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurassic "Jurassic"), after the global [Toarcian Oceanic Anoxic Event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toarcian_Oceanic_Anoxic_Event "Toarcian Oceanic Anoxic Event") there was a diversification of dinoflagellates and coccolithophores, in both species and abundance. This interval also saw the completion of a symbiosis between [Acantharia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acantharia "Acantharia") radiolarians and lineages of _[Phaeocystis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phaeocystis "Phaeocystis")_ haptophytes, as well as the appearance of planktonic foraminifera.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224) The period of low atmospheric oxygen ends in the [Aptian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aptian "Aptian")-[Albian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albian "Albian") boundary during the Early [Cretaceous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cretaceous "Cretaceous"), and the first fossils of diatoms and silicoflagellates appear.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224) Samples of [amber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amber "Amber") from around 100 Ma contain the oldest fossil records of [apicomplexans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apicomplexa "Apicomplexa") (particularly [malarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria") agents and [gregarines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregarine "Gregarine")), [trypanosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trypanosomatida "Trypanosomatida"),[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Leung-2017-256) and [metamonads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamonad "Metamonad")â€”particularly mutualistic [parabasalids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parabasalid "Parabasalid") of [cockroaches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cockroaches "Cockroaches"), representing the earliest record of mutualism between protists and animals.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Poinar-2009-257)[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Poinar-2009b-258)

The diversification of coccolithophores, mixotrophic dinoflagellates, and later diatoms across the Mesozoic era caused an accelerated transfer of primary production into higher trophic levels. This evolutionary radiation of phytoplankton was, in turn, responsible for the animal "Mesozoic marine revolution", characterized by the appearance of widespread predation among most invertebrate phyla. Coccolithophores, dinoflagellates and especially diatoms became the dominating eukaryotic producers in oceans until today, as opposed to [cyanobacteria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanobacteria "Cyanobacteria") and green algae which dominated earlier.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-259)

The [Cretaceous-Paleogene extinction event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cretaceous-Paleogene_extinction_event "Cretaceous-Paleogene extinction event") (~66 Ma) caused the extinction of many marine dinoflagellates, foraminifers, coccolithophores, and silicoflagellates; mesozoic types of these groups were substituted with types that dominate marine habitats today. Right after this event, putative [ebridians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebriid "Ebriid") begin appearing in the fossil record (e.g., _[Ammodochium](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ammodochium&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ammodochium (page does not exist)")_), but the oldest reliable ebridian fossils belong to the upper middle [Eocene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eocene "Eocene") (42â€“33.7 Ma).[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224) Around this time, the oldest fossils of [Synurophyceae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synurophyceae "Synurophyceae") appear (~49â€“40 Ma).[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Brown-2010-260) Following the [Middle Eocene Climatic Optimum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Eocene_Climatic_Optimum "Middle Eocene Climatic Optimum") (~40 Ma), diatoms became the dominant agents of marine silicon precipitation as opposed to radiolarians, and the fossil record shows the first raphid diatoms and [collodarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collodaria "Collodaria").[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Suzuki-2015-224)

1.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-kingdoms_13-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-kingdoms_13-1)The distinction between protists and the other three eukaryotic kingdoms has been difficult to settle. Historically, the [heterotrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterotroph "Heterotroph") protists, known as [protozoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protozoa "Protozoa"), were considered part of the [animal kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal"), while the [phototrophic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phototroph "Phototroph") ones, called [algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae "Algae"), were studied as part of the [plant kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant_kingdom "Plant kingdom"). Even after the creation of a separate protist kingdom, some minuscule animals (the [myxozoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myxozoa "Myxozoa"))[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Levine-1980-6) and 'lower' [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungi "Fungi") (namely the [aphelids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphelida "Aphelida"), [rozellids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rozellida "Rozellida") and [microsporidians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsporidia "Microsporidia"), collectively known as [Opisthosporidia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opisthosporidia "Opisthosporidia")) were studied as protists,[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-7)[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-8)[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2022-9) and some algae (particularly [red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_algae "Red algae") and [green algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_algae "Green algae")) remained classified as plants.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-1998-10) According to the current consensus, the label 'protist' specifically excludes animals, [embryophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embryophyte "Embryophyte") (land plants) â€”meaning that all algae fall under this labelâ€” and all fungi. Opisthosporidians are considered part of a larger fungal kingdom, although they are often studied by [protistologists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protistologist "Protistologist") and [mycologists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mycologist "Mycologist") alike.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Tedersoo-2018-11)[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Wijayawardene-2022-12)
2.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-cilia_28-0)**The terms '[cilium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cilium "Cilium")' and '[eukaryotic flagellum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryotic_flagellum "Eukaryotic flagellum")' are interchangeable from a biological perspective. However, their usage depends on the author: some prefer to reserve cilia for shorter appendages and flagella for longer ones, while others prefer cilia for eukaryotes and flagella for prokaryotes. The term '[undulipodium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undulipodium "Undulipodium")' was proposed to unify the two concepts, as it refers specifically to the [homologous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homology_(biology) "Homology (biology)")[microtubular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microtubular "Microtubular") structure found in both, but not found in [prokaryotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prokaryotic "Prokaryotic") flagella.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-25)[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-26)[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-27)
3.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-39)**A 2007 report on protist diversity included a table listing the described number of species for protist and fungal groups. The total sum of the listed species, excluding fungi, is 76,144.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2007-38)
4.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-Percolozoa_50-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-Percolozoa_50-1)The phylum Percolozoa is usually better known as Heterolobosea.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Adl-2019-2)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-P%C3%A1nek-2017-49) However, in the strictest sense, Heterolobosea refers only to a class within this phylum, containing the orders [Acrasida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acrasida "Acrasida") and [Schizopyrenida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schizopyrenida "Schizopyrenida"). The name Percolozoa encompasses these and other related single-celled protists, not just the 'true' heteroloboseans.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Cavalier-Smith-2022-9)
5.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-156)**The terms "mixotroph" and "mixoplankton" almost exclusively refer to protists that perform photosynthesis and phagocytosis (photo-phagotrophs). Osmotrophy is always present, but not taken into account. As such, "pure" phototrophs (incapable of phagocytosis) and "pure" phagotrophs (incapable of photosynthesis) are technically mixotrophic due to their innate ability for osmotrophy, but are not usually reported in this sense.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-155)
6.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-201)**[Carl von Linnaeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_von_Linnaeus "Carl von Linnaeus") did not mention a single protist genus until the tenth edition of _[Systema Naturae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systema\_Naturae "Systema Naturae")_ of 1758, where _[Volvox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvox "Volvox")_ was recorded.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Leadbeater-2000-200)
7.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_ref-223)**In 2015, Cavalier-Smith's initial six-kingdom model was revised into a [seven-kingdom model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)#Seven_kingdoms "Kingdom (biology)") after the inclusion of [Archaea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaea "Archaea").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protist#cite_note-Ruggiero-2015-222)

### Physiology, ecology and paleontology

*   Fontaneto, D. _Biogeography of Microscopic Organisms. Is Everything Small Everywhere?_ Cambridge University Press, Cambridge, 2011.
